The Issue of Ironware Freight Charges: German-Polish Agreement. Germany Agrees to Pay Freight, Partially in Goods. 74

(Berlin) Regarding the issue of railway freight charges for German goods passing through the Polish Corridor, which has been disputed between the two countries for a long time, the governments of Germany and Poland recently signed an agreement to resolve it. According to the agreement, Germany will pay railway freight charges, partly in foreign currency and partly in goods. It is said that the German side insists on paying part of the freight in goods due to a shortage of foreign currency. (Note: Since the European War, a corridor has been demarcated between the province of East Prussia and the western part of Germany, called the Polish Corridor. Germany previously concluded an agreement with Poland to facilitate the transit of goods, stipulating that Germany would pay Poland 3,200,000 złoty per month in Polish currency as transit fees for trains. Subsequently, Germany repeatedly defaulted on payments, claiming that its foreign currency reserves were low, and the accumulated arrears amounted to 570,000,000 złoty. In addition, this agreement was due to expire at the end of December this year, so the two sides began negotiations to settle the old debts on the one hand and establish a new payment method on the other. An agreement has now been reached.) (Havas, 22nd)

U.S. Government Studies New Neutrality Law 76

(Washington) Regarding the new neutrality bill that President Roosevelt plans to submit to Congress, Senator Borah, former chairman of the Senate Foreign Relations Committee, recently told the press that this bill is intended to supplement the existing neutrality law (which will expire at the end of February next year) so that it can also be applied in the event of civil wars in various countries. Its content is as follows: (1) Strictly prohibit the transport of munitions to belligerent countries; (2) Prohibit the lending of funds to belligerent countries; (3) Prohibit American citizens from traveling on belligerent-owned ships. As for ordinary commerce, President Roosevelt should decide at his discretion, and there is no need to stipulate it in the new neutrality bill. (Havas, 22nd)

Anglo-Egyptian Treaty Takes Effect: Sir Lampson Appointed British Ambassador to Egypt. He Played a Major Role in the Treaty's Completion. 77

(London) Following the signing of the Anglo-Egyptian Treaty of Friendship and Alliance in Cairo yesterday, the British government today appointed Sir Miles Lampson, Commissioner for Egypt and Sudan, as the second British Ambassador to Egypt. Lampson played a significant role in the completion of the treaty. After seventeen years of protracted negotiations between the two countries, the treaty was finally concluded, thus placing the relations between the two countries on a solid foundation. Since Italy's conquest of Abyssinia, a new situation has emerged in the Near East, greatly changing the situation in the Mediterranean. Egypt, because its 800-mile border with Sudan is adjacent to Italy's new territory, felt disturbed. In 1935, without consulting Sir Miles Lampson, it asked the British government to reopen the negotiations that had broken down in 1930. After the British Foreign Office agreed, it appointed Lampson to take on this task and assisted him with senior technical experts from the army, navy, and air force. After taking office, Lampson devoted himself to his duties, adapting to the needs of the situation, applying both firmness and flexibility. When Egypt made excessive demands, Lampson told them in a calm and firm manner that if the negotiations failed, there would be serious consequences, and Britain would be forced to reconsider its policy towards Egypt, so Egypt made concessions. When Egypt declared that it could make no further concessions, Lampson took a plane to London and strongly urged the Foreign Office to also make concessions to preserve the overall situation. After six months of arduous work, the treaty was finally concluded, winning the praise of the majority of the people of both Britain and Egypt. Lampson's contribution is truly indispensable, so the British government awarded him the post of Ambassador to Egypt to reward his merits. (Reuters, 23rd)

Duke of Windsor's Wedding Date: Approximately in April Next Year. Lovers Finally Get Married. 78

Enzesfeld A reporter from the Associated Press learned today from reliable sources that Mrs. Simpson, for whom the British Duke of Windsor, formerly King Edward, sacrificed the throne, will become the Duchess of Windsor before May next year. The Duke is currently residing at the home of Count Rothschild and does not intend to meet with Mrs. Simpson until after the marriage. (National Telegram, 22nd)

Invoking the Escalator Clause: Retaining Old Warships. Britain Formally Notifies the U.S. and Japan. 80

(London) The British Foreign Office issued formal notices to the U.S. and Japanese embassies in Britain this afternoon, stating that the British government has decided to invoke Article 21 of the 1930 London Naval Treaty, the escalator clause, to retain five cruisers (totaling 21,000 tons) that have reached their service age without dismantling them. The retention period shall not exceed five years in peacetime. These cruisers will now be converted with 6-inch caliber guns for use as anti-aircraft ships. The armor on the ships will also be replaced and will no longer be suitable for long-distance ocean navigation. It is reported that the Japanese government notified the British government before the issuance of this notice that it had no objection to Britain retaining five cruisers that had reached the end of their service life. However, it is generally expected that the Japanese side will also issue a similar notice, declaring that 26,000 tons of submarines and cruisers that should be dismantled will still be retained. (Havas, 22nd)

(London) The five cruisers retained by the British naval authorities a few days ago will be converted into "anti-aircraft ships," each equipped with an aircraft landing field, anti-aircraft guns, and all anti-aircraft designs. This plan has been notified to the governments of the United States and Japan. (National Telegram, 22nd)

New Developments in Japan's Southern Advance Strategy: Zhongnan Joint Stock Company Established in Shantou. Will Control the Freight Business in Chaozhou and Meizhou. 84

Shantou Correspondence: Japan's southern advance policy, with economics as the vanguard, Taiwan as the base, and the coastal areas of Fujian and Guangdong as the target of advance, has been proceeding very rapidly recently. As evidenced by the establishment of the Taiwan Colonization Company last month and the subsequent birth of the Shantou Zhongnan Joint Stock Company. The Shantou Zhongnan Joint Stock Company is located at the former Daito Swimming Factory on Shen Zhao Road, Qi Qiang, next to the Japanese Consulate. On the 9th of this month, Huang Xin, a Taiwanese councilor sent by the Governor-General's Office of Taiwan, arrived in Shantou to guide everything. On the 11th, Huang hosted a banquet for the Japanese consul and invited well-known Japanese and Taiwanese figures in Shantou to hold the company's inauguration ceremony at the Shantou Tao Fang Garden. It is said that the company is extraordinarily large in scale and has the intention of monopolizing the freight business in the Chaozhou and Meizhou regions. The Chaozhou and Shantou North-South port transportation, grain, seafood, Beijing confectionery, and various industry associations are extremely fearful. The company's business scope is divided into five departments: (1) Grain Department: Contracted with the Mitsubishi Company of Northeast China to transport and sell soybeans, soybean oil, peanut kernels, bean cakes, and other special products of Northeast China. All products produced by Japanese commercial factories in Northeast China will be managed and sold by Zhongnan Company; (2) Seafood Department: Dedicated to selling fresh fish, salted fish, dried fish, and all seafood products on behalf of the largest joint fishery company in Japan, the Hong Kong Penglai Fishery Company, etc.; (3) Matches and Cotton Yarn: Agents for the promotion and sale of matches produced in Northeast China by Mitsui Yangxing and cotton yarn and all textiles and artificial silk produced by Japanese yarn factories in China; (4) Sundries Department: Transport and sell all products produced by various Japanese light and heavy industrial factories; (5) Transit Department: Transport raw materials produced in various parts of China to Japan for use in Japanese factories. For example, tungsten, antimony, manganese, iron, tin, lead and other minerals, as well as rosin, Sansheng, duck and goose feathers produced in Chaozhou and Shantou are all included in the sales. The company has established a general office in Shantou and branches in Chaoan and Jieyang counties. It competes with the original scattered and unorganized Chinese businessmen with huge funds and cheap goods, and with the Taiwan Development Company as a backing and the Taiwan Bank as a support, the development of its future is not optimistic for our Chinese businessmen. In addition, the company plans to start business on New Year's Day next year and has hired Mr. Li as an agent. Li is a first-class real seller. They have also secretly sent people to Puning, Jieyang, Wuhua, Meixian and other tungsten mining production areas to investigate and purchase mineral sand, and plan to apply to the Construction Department for mining rights in the name of Chinese. On the 13th, the company and Osaka Shosen Co., Ltd. chartered three ships dedicated to transporting the company's goods back and forth between Taiwan, Xiamen, Shantou, Dalian, Yingkou, Qingdao, and Shantou. In the future, in addition to distributing the company's goods to various Japanese ships for transportation to Shantou, these three special ships will be used as assistance. From then on, the economic power of a certain country will definitely become more fierce. In addition, the company relies on three things: (1) The cost of goods shipped is low; (2) The freight of ships and fire markets is particularly favorable; (3) When goods are in Shantou, in addition to paying regular taxes to the customs, no other special taxes are paid. According to this calculation, it is difficult for Chinese businessmen to compete with the enemy, so all Chinese businessmen are discouraged by what they hear.

Repairing the Ye Pond to Commend Loyalty and Martyrdom 85

Jiadong Correspondence: The county government believes that Hou Tongzeng, a martyr of this county, advocated defending the city during the Ming-Yi Dynasty transition. On the day the city was breached, he and his sons Yan and Jie died in the Ye Pond of his home and garden. The pond is located in the northwest alley of the city in front of the current county junior vocational school. The eastern half has been filled in as a flat ground, and the western half is also quite silted up. The county has specially submitted a report to the province for approval to use public funds to repair it in order to preserve the historical site and commemorate the martyrs. The pond land was originally contracted by the Fang and Lu families for grain. After hearing the news, they voluntarily donated it to the public, and the county government commended them. Construction began in the autumn and has now been completed. The pond is surrounded by a wooden fence, with iron buckets built in front and the words "Ye Pond" marked on the door. The couplet on both sides reads, "Selling hatred in the clear pond, the blue blood and cold ripples dissolve into one piece; donating life to complete the great festival, loyal ministers and filial sons each for thousands of years." It was written by County Mayor Guo Mingnian. A stone monument is erected at a distance of more than ten feet from the entrance, surrounded by stone paths. The rest of the land in the fence above the pond is planted with trees.

Black Pottery Cultural Site Discovered in Hang County. Numerous Artifacts, Dating Back to Before the Yin and Shang Dynasties. 88

Hangzhou Correspondence: Shi Xinshi, a member of the West Lake Museum, recently discovered many Black Pottery cultural sites in Hang County while investigating the county's geology. The sites were found at the bottom of the pond, two meters from the surface, contained within a layer of black silt. The artifacts include pottery gui, dou, ding, bu, ping, min, basin, pan, etc., in numerous forms, all with primitive forms of Shang and Zhou bronzes. The shapes and techniques are quite exquisite, with a pitch-black luster, brittle and delicate. According to the Black Pottery cultural sites, which were first discovered at the Chengziya site in Longshan Town, Licheng, Shandong, archaeologists believe that they are an inherent culture of the ancient East and an important component of the earliest historical period of Chinese culture, dating back to before the Yin and Shang Dynasties. This culture originated on the coast of the East and gradually moved westward. It has also been discovered in the ruins of Henan, etc. Compared to the general emphasis on the external origin of ancient Chinese culture as being purely from the West, this is a great change. It has now been discovered in the South, with the evidence on the stratum and the comparison of objects, there is no distinction between high and low, it is no less than showing the traces of cultural development and communication in our ancient coastal plain area. For Zhejiang, which lacks historical materials, even more valuable material evidence has been obtained, so it makes a great contribution to academic research. According to Mr. Shi's repeated investigations in the Hang County area, the underground situation of the stratum has gradually become clear. Mr. Shi also said that the ancient cultural layers of Hang County can be roughly divided into three periods: the early period represents the Neolithic Age, with various crude stone tools, such as unperforated stone axes, stone scalpers, stone halberds, stone arrowheads, stone adzes, stone yue, and stone sickles; the middle period represents the end of the Stone-Copper Age, that is, the recently discovered Black Pottery culture, which also has stone tools, which are made with exquisite workmanship; the late period represents the Spring and Autumn Period, the Warring States Period, and the early Han Dynasty, when the culture was already fully developed, with the most prominent being the groups of pottery fragments with engraved patterns and printed patterns. There are more than 20 kinds of geometric patterns on the pottery fragments, which are distributed in three areas of Hang County. In addition to the pottery fragment groups, there are also well-known Han jade and many stone gui that have been unearthed, which are the characteristics of this period.

It is also heard that the West Lake Museum is currently engaged in research due to the large amount of materials obtained, and a report will be published. The actual objects such as black pottery stone tools will also be sorted and publicly displayed in the museum's history and culture department for reference by all walks of life.

Wuxi: Zhenxin Factory Prepares to Resume Operations 91

The Zhenxin Yarn Factory, located at Taibaodun outside the West Gate, is managed by local resident Jiang Zheqing. It has suffered significant losses over the years. All of the factory's assets, totaling more than 900,000 yuan, are mortgaged to the Shanghai Bank. In addition, it also owes debts of more than 190,000 yuan to banks such as the China Bank and the Central South Bank. It suspended operations last summer because it was unable to maintain them. Subsequently, the yarn factory's situation gradually improved. After several rounds of consultations, it was still unable to resume operations. Most recently, Chairman of the Board Dai Lucen and General Manager of the Shanghai Bank Chen Guangfu repeatedly discussed the matter and came up with concrete solutions. Zou Bingwen from the Shanghai Bank and representative lawyer Qiu Fenling came to Wuxi to jointly negotiate with Qian Sunqing, chairman of the Chamber of Commerce. It has been decided that: (1) After the factory resumes operations, all working capital will be advanced by the Shanghai Bank. The funds for repairing machinery, estimated at more than 110,000 yuan, will also be advanced by the Shanghai Bank. (2) The interest on the advances and old debts will be reduced to 7% per annum, a decrease of 1% from before. All profits from the factory will be used to repay the debts, and the Shanghai Bank will not share in the profits. The above measures have been formally contracted, and the Shanghai Bank has dispatched Yang Guanbei, manager of the Shanghai Great Northern Shipping Company, to Wuxi to make contact. At the same time, the county government has also received an order from the provincial government to protect the factory's resumption of operations. County Magistrate Long convened a meeting at the county government yesterday afternoon, bringing together all relevant parties to discuss the handover procedures.

Bengbu: Resumption of Huai River Transportation 94

Since the beginning of autumn, northern Anhui has suffered from a prolonged drought. The water level of the Huai River has gradually decreased. Ships traveling to and from Zhengyang in the upper reaches have been at risk of running aground, causing the interruption of transportation and adversely affecting shipping businesses. Since the heavy rains and initial snowfall a few days ago, the water level of the Huai River has risen sharply by more than two chi [unit of measurement, roughly one-third of a meter]. Long-distance ships traveling from here to Zhengyang resumed their scheduled runs on the morning of the 22nd. Small boats from both Bengbu and Zhengyang will operate daily. Small boats from Bengbu to Wuhe in the lower reaches will also begin operating within days to facilitate merchants and travelers and benefit transportation.

The "Popularization" Movement of Reading Materials 95

— Special Correspondence from Beiping

The "popularization" movement of people's education materials has existed in the capital area for several years. However, it only truly became a trend and flourished when the Popular Reading Materials Compilation and Publication Society significantly expanded its scale this year. Despite the twists and turns and evolving developments, and although it largely relied on the painstaking support of a few scholars in terms of subjective factors, the needs of China's objective social environment in recent years have been the biggest factor in the flourishing of this movement. After the slogan of "Popularization of Literature and Art" was put forward in Shanghai around 1929 and 1930, Beiping also responded. Combined with the enlightenment spirit since the May Fourth Movement, it emerged in a different form, which is the so-called "popularization." Therefore, in spirit, the "popularization" movement in Beiping is still a continuation of the enlightenment spirit of the "May Fourth" Movement, but it appeared with a new look under the stimulation of the "popularization" movement in Shanghai. The difference between "popularization" and the enlightenment movement lies in the essence and purpose, and the difference between "popularization" and "popularization" lies in the spirit and method. If we still advocate the enlightenment movement of the "May Fourth" era today, it would be insufficient. However, those who advocate "popularization" often encounter practical conflicts and obstacles in terms of methods and spirit. Therefore, in the current situation in our country, it is necessary to pay attention to the "popularization" movement, which aims to educate the people with new content based on the spirit of enlightenment. Therefore, I have recorded the information I have gathered as follows:

(1) The Movement to "Popularize" Reading Materials

The most important organization engaged in this movement is the Popular Reading Materials Compilation and Publication Society. It was established as early as five years ago, but in the past, due to lack of funds, limited personnel, and no fixed address, it was only supported by a few enthusiasts with the support of enthusiastic scholars. Its work was also limited to collecting old reading materials popular among the people, compiling and classifying them. In terms of various ballad forms alone, it is said that there are already more than one or two thousand types. In terms of publication, it only published a few publications and single volumes under the names of other cultural organizations within the scope of its capabilities, and the circulation was not wide. Since this year, the scale has gradually increased. It now has a fixed address, located at No. 7 Guanyinchang, Beiping, with more than ten rooms, and has established editing, publishing, and other departments, with a total of more than ten staff and workers. The reporter visited the society and saw that its work was very intense. Currently, the society's source of funds is still very difficult. It mainly relies on donations and subsidies from various parties. For example, Luo Jialun, president of National Central University, recently donated 500 yuan. A month or so ago, it was reported that the society had submitted a request to the Hebei-Chahar authorities for subsidies, but there has been no further news since then.

In addition to the Popular Reading Materials Compilation and Publication Society, the Beiping Research Institute and other cultural organizations are also enthusiastic about this "popularization" movement. There are also many individuals who are enthusiastic about supporting it.

(2) A Glimpse of "Popularized" People's Reading Materials

According to the reporter's investigation, the organizations and individuals engaged in the "popularization" movement are indeed considering the fact that there is a large illiterate population among our people. At the same time, given that the popularization of education and the improvement of Chinese characters are not achievable in the short term, those who want to educate the people with new knowledge, in addition to using text, can only rely on methods such as pictures, shadow plays, and ballads. However, due to funding and other limitations, the training of ballad singers and shadow play performers has only been planned so far and has not yet been implemented. The achievements so far are only in the two aspects of compiling and publishing reading materials and printing pictures.

More than ten kinds of reading materials have been compiled and published. Roughly speaking, periodicals such as "People's Weekly" and "Popular Knowledge" (bi-monthly) are either printed by the Popular Reading Materials Compilation and Publication Society itself or entrusted to the Shanghai Yadong Library for printing. The former uses simple language to introduce the people to various common knowledge of international and domestic politics, society, and economics, as well as knowledge of science, history, and geography. For example, in its inaugural issue, it translated a Shenyang correspondence from this newspaper on September 19 from classical Chinese into simple vernacular, so that the people who do not have the opportunity to read the newspaper can also learn about the situation of the Japanese oppression of our compatriots in the Northeast provinces, which is one example. The latter specializes in publishing systematic papers, but once it is systematically established, the text will inevitably be more profound. However, its ultimate goal is to move towards popularization. The series of books can be divided into two types, A and B. The content of the A series of books mainly focuses on common sense of natural science, common sense of social science, historical and geographical narratives, biographies of famous people, and story novels. Those already published include eight or nine kinds such as "Dayu's Selflessness," "Goujian's Revenge on Wu," and "Cao Mo's Revenge." The purpose is to replace the harmful and unsound reading materials popular among the people with this kind of reading materials, such as "Seven Heroes and Five Gallants" and "The Cases of Shi Gong." The content of the B series of books is similar to that of the A series, but the style is in the form of ballads, old drama lyrics, folk songs, and ditties. More than sixty kinds have been published so far. These can be divided into (1) National Humiliation category, such as "Du Quan's Death to Defend Dujiayu," "Hu Amao Drives a Car in Huangpu," "Making a Scene at Zhaojialou," etc. (2) Social category, such as "White-Faced Ghost," etc. (3) Education category, such as "The Blind Man with Eyes," etc. (4) History and Geography category, such as "Song Zheyuan's Great Battle at Xifengkou," "The Battle of Shanghai," etc. The purpose of this series of books is to replace the more basic and also the most widely circulated unsound reading materials among the people, such as "Crying at Five Watches" and "The Prostitute's Sad Autumn." The cover and inside pages of the books are attached with many meaningful illustrations in a new style. The price is low and reprinting is not strictly prohibited. In addition to periodicals and series of books, those that appear in newspapers in the form of supplements are also common. The most notable ones are the "Popular Lecture" in this newspaper's supplement, "Folk Customs" in the Central Daily News's supplement, "Life and Education" in the Beiping Morning News, "Social Science" and "Modern Children" in the World Daily News, "Popular Forum" in the North China Daily, "Popular Education" in the Real News, "Folklore Weekly" in the People's Voice, and "Citizens' Weekly" in the New Beiping Daily, etc. Although their content, writing style, and attitude are different, the same purpose is to promote the "popularization" movement of reading materials. It is of great significance that they have appeared one after another in a new style during the flourishing of this movement.

In terms of paintings, considerable achievements have also been made. Although the form is still the same as the old New Year pictures, etc., not only is the content meaningful, but also the style is completely new and cannot be compared with the unsound and decadent New Year pictures of the past. Dozens of paintings have already been reprinted and are being printed. According to the content, it can be divided into (1) Historical Story category, such as "The Biography of Yue Fei," "Ban Chao Throws His Pen," etc. (2) Women's Life category, such as "Spring, Summer, Autumn, and Winter of Farm Women's Life," etc. (3) Children's Education category, such as "Descendants Forever," etc. (4) Public Life category, such as "Seventy-Two Trades Eight Pictures," "Spring, Summer, Autumn, and Winter of Farm Life," etc. (5) Drama category, such as "Killing the Family by Fishing," etc. (6) Humorous Satire and Persuasion category, such as "The Snipe and the Clam Fight," "The Story of Gambler Wang Da," etc. (7) Breaking Superstition category, such as "The God of Wealth," "The God of Longevity," "The Celestial Official," "Zhong Kui," etc. (8) Scenic Spots category, such as "Beihai and Summer Palace of Beiping," etc. (9) Patriotic Story category, such as "Yao Ruifang, the Female General of the Righteous Army" and "The Martyrdom of Cuihong Girl." Each painting is exquisitely printed, the brushwork is sophisticated, and the price is low. They are all unprecedented and can be considered meaningful. The inscriptions on each painting are particularly noteworthy. Here are a few excerpts to give a glimpse, such as the inscription on Farm Life: "Our country has 400 million people, farmers account for the majority. No one cares about the bankruptcy of the countryside, the whole country is going to be finished." Inscription on Seventy-Two Trades: "There are many businesses in the seventy-two trades, each earns money and lives their own life. Everyone is united to buy domestic goods, the country is peaceful and the people are happy." Inscription on Children's Education: "Little baby is well-born, loves to read and loves to play. Not afraid of bullets and cannons, only afraid of foreigners laughing at me." Inscription on Women's Life in Winter: "The north wind is blowing in winter, you weave cloth and she spins cotton. If all compatriots can work hard, why should the country worry about no financial resources?"

Overview of National Libraries in the 24th Year 106

The Ministry of Education compiled an overview of national public and private libraries in the 19th year of the Republic. Subsequently, in February of the 24th year, it distributed forms to various provinces and cities to investigate the current status of libraries. After much delay, the results of the investigation have now been compiled into the most recent statistics: (1) The total number of school libraries nationwide is 1,963, an increase of 1,269 compared to the 19th year, representing a twofold increase. (Guangdong has 223, Hubei 221, Shanghai 172, Jiangsu 120, Hebei 152, Zhejiang 111, Peiping 86, Anhui 80, Shandong 89, Henan 74, Shanxi 72, Fujian 98, Guangxi 89, Hunan 54, Sichuan 62, Yunnan 53, Shaanxi 49, Jiangxi 47, and the rest range from 26 to a dozen or even one or two.) (2) The total number of public libraries nationwide is 1,255, an increase of 680 compared to before, representing an increase of more than one time. (Hebei has 148, Zhejiang 147, Shandong 131, Jiangsu 102, Henan 102, Hunan 69, Anhui 52, Hubei 43, Shanxi 5, Fujian 44, Guangdong 49, Yunnan 73, Shaanxi 29, Jiangxi 28, Sichuan and Gansu each have 24, Guangxi 23, and the rest are within 10.) (3) The total number of government libraries nationwide is 173, an increase of half compared to before. (Shanghai has 37, Beijing 36, Zhejiang 28, Hubei 12, and the rest range from 7 or 8 to one or two.) (4) The total number of private libraries nationwide is 20, an increase of two and a half times compared to before. (Zhejiang has 5, Hubei and Yunnan each have 3, Shanxi and Anhui each have 2, Peiping, Qingdao, Jiangxi, and Suiyuan each have 1.) (5) The total number of circulating libraries nationwide is 37. (Hebei has 14, Jiangsu 8, Hubei and Yunnan each have 4, Shanghai and Zhejiang each have 2, Jiangxi, Shanxi, and Shaanxi each have 1.) (6) The total number of specialized libraries nationwide is 11, a decrease of 47 compared to before. (Beijing has 2, Shanghai, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Jiangxi, Sichuan, Shanxi, Gansu, and Fujian each have 1.) (7) The total number of general libraries nationwide is 573, a decrease of 330 compared to before. (Guangdong has 50, Guangxi 45, Sichuan 78, Jiangsu 27, Zhejiang 28, Anhui 17, Jiangxi 15, Hebei 12, Henan 43, Shanxi 24, Shaanxi 18, Gansu 23, Fujian 30, Guizhou 23, Yunnan 12, and the rest are below 10.) In terms of each type of library, school libraries, public libraries, private libraries, and government libraries have all increased year by year, while general libraries have sharply decreased. In terms of the location of the libraries, there are 4,032 libraries nationwide, an increase of one-half compared to before. Among the special municipalities and special regions directly under the central government, Shanghai has the most libraries, with 229, followed by Peiping, with 107, then Beijing, with 56, Qingdao with 13, and Weihaiwei with the fewest, only 3. Among the provinces, Hebei has the most libraries, with 320, followed by Guangdong, with 325, then Zhejiang, with 322. Xinjiang and Xikang have the fewest, with only 1. Generally speaking, Guangdong, Hunan, Ningxia, Henan, Jiangsu, and Shandong provinces have all increased compared to before, with Guangxi Province increasing the most, by seven times, followed by Chahar, by five times, Jiangxi, Shanxi, Hubei, and Qingdao by three times, Shanghai, Anhui, and Sichuan by more than two times, Suiyuan by one and a half times, Hebei by more than one time, Gansu, Zhejiang, and Shaanxi by one-third, Fujian by two-fifths, and Guizhou by one-fifth. The rest, Beijing and Peiping, have each increased by one-fifth. Xikang and Xinjiang have not seen any increase or decrease.

Shanghai Boy Scout Wartime Service Corps Begins Recruiting Members; Registration Deadline Set for the End of This Month; Female Youths Temporarily Not Accepted 107

The Shanghai Boy Scout Wartime Service Corps, since its preparation, has lasted for many days. After several meetings of the Shanghai Boy Scout Council, the Corps' regulations and procedures were approved. The Corps' officers have all been appointed. Now that preparations are complete, it has been decided to begin recruiting members from today. The registration period is from the 22nd to the 31st of this month. Centralized training will begin next month. In addition to announcing the news in the Shen Bao, Xin Bao, and other newspapers, notices have been sent to various groups to recruit members. The Corps' regulations have been printed. Those interested in participating can come for a personal consultation. The recruitment rules are listed below: (1) Purpose: To promote the spirit of the Boy Scouts and serve the country during wartime. (2) Qualifications: Male individuals with one of the following qualifications are eligible to apply (female youths are temporarily not accepted): (A) Members of Shanghai Boy Scout groups who are 16 years of age or older. (B) Shanghai Boy Scout service personnel. (C) Youths from all walks of life who are 16 to 25 years of age and have received secondary education. (3) Registration Period: From December 22nd to 31st. (4) Registration Location: Within the Shanghai Special Municipality Council of the China Boy Scouts, at Dajilu, Ximen. (5) Enrollment Procedures: The individual must personally have their scout leader submit the volunteer form and investigation form. After filling them out, attach two 2.5-inch half-body photos and submit them to the Corps. Those who pass the review will be notified to participate in the exam. After passing the exam, a guarantor must be found before enrollment.

The Shanghai General Examination concluded on the 16th of this month with the third test. After review, a total of 26 people were deemed qualified, as reported in previous newspapers. Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education Rectifies Teachers in Private Schools 111

Orders each county to select students to send to the province for training, After completion of the training, they are assigned to serve in the private schools of each county. The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education recently received an order from the Provincial Government to establish another teacher training class for private schools in the provincial capital for the purpose of supplementing and rectifying the teachers of the people's schools. It also formulated and issued to various county bureaus for compliance and selection of students from each county. The quota is determined by the number of private schools in each county. After the two-month training period, the Department of Education will assign them to serve in various counties. Procedures for each county to send students should be reported to the province by January 8, 26th year, arrive at the Department for re-examination on the 14th, and classes will begin on the 20th. The regulations for sending students to the teacher training class for private schools are listed below: (1) Quota: A total of 200 places, to be selected by the Education Bureau of each county (or the county government in counties where the bureau has been abolished) according to the following standards after examination and sent to the province for re-examination: (A) For central private schools and township private schools totaling between 10 and 20, send 2 to 4 students. (B) For central private schools and township private schools totaling between 20 and 30, send 4 to 6 students. (C) For central private schools and township private schools totaling between 30 and 40, send 5 to 8 students. (D) For central private schools and township private schools totaling over 40, send 8 to 12 students. (2) Qualifications: Students sent must possess the following qualifications: (A) Males aged 20 to 30 years. (B) Graduates of senior high school or above. (C) Strong physique, pure thoughts, and no bad habits. Graduates of teacher training institutes in various districts who have not yet been assigned duties, and graduates of junior high schools or above, may also be selected and sent by each county. (3) Examination: Students sent to the province will be subject to the following examinations: (A) Physical examination. (B) Written examination: Party principles, Chinese language, Chinese history and geography, current affairs, outline of education, and military common sense. (C) Oral examination. Those who fail the physical examination will not be allowed to take the written examination. (4) Period: The training period is three months. (5) Treatment: The treatment of the sent students is as follows: (A) Travel expenses are borne by the students themselves. (B) Food expenses, uniform expenses, and applied books during the training period are provided by the training class. (6) Procedures: (A) Each candidate should prepare two 4-inch half-body photos, together with their school graduation certificate (students of teacher training institutes should also submit their graduation certificate from the training institute) and submit them to the Education Bureau (or the county government in counties where the bureau has been abolished). (B) The Education Bureau (or the county government in counties where the bureau has been abolished) should send the photos of the sent students (the name, age, native place, and graduating school of the student should be written on the back of the photo, and the Education Bureau (or the county magistrate in counties where the bureau has been abolished) should sign and stamp it), together with the student's application form, to the Provincial Department of Education for review by express mail before January 8, 26th year, without delay. (7) Dates: (A) Students sent from each county should report to the province for re-examination on January 14, 26th year. (B) Training will begin on January 20th. (8) Service: Students who pass the examination after the training period will be assigned by the Department of Education to serve in the people's schools of various counties.

Current Status of the Shanghai Municipal Library; Catalog of Books and Magazines Also Published 112

The Shanghai Municipal Library in the city center, since its trial opening on September 1st, has seen an increasing number of readers. Over 5,200 people visited the library in October, with Sundays being the busiest. Although the book and magazine reading rooms were closed for several days in November due to repairs, the number of readers still reached over 5,500. The library, in order to benefit scholars, has opened all the radiators in the reading rooms since the beginning of this week, bringing spring to the entire room, which is good news for readers. The first volume of the catalog of books and magazines (Chinese and Western languages combined) has also been published. The entire book is arranged according to classification numbers, with the cover bearing an inscription by the Mayor. The book has 290+ pages. It is said that schools, institutions, and organizations in need can request it with an official letter. All the librarians, under the leadership of Director Hong, are working hard and diligently. Recently, a Chinese and Western language cataloging committee has been organized to speed up the work, with the aim of preparing for the official opening in a short period of time. Efforts are also being made to perfect the facilities. The second-floor hall has been renovated to serve as a rest area for readers. In addition, in order to facilitate readers who wish to read books at the library all day, the library has contacted the municipal government's kitchen to provide lunch on behalf of the readers. It is also said that copper reading cards will be used starting in January 26th. Everything is being done to strive for excellence, which shows the Municipal Government's determination to vigorously develop cultural construction.

Social Bureau Orders Subordinates to Solicit Donations to Aid Suiyuan; to be Handed Over to the Cultural Circles Support Association; Designated Institutions 113

Since the bandit-puppets invaded Suiyuan, our army has fought bravely and achieved frequent victories. In order to actively assist the soldiers on the front lines and to fulfill their national duty of defending the country, the various social groups and institutions in the Shanghai cultural community have established the Cultural Circles Suiyuan Bandit Suppression Support Association. This association oversees all matters related to the Suiyuan aid movement within the Shanghai cultural community. In order to concentrate efforts and unify planning, in addition to the one-day salary deduction for faculty and staff of municipal schools, which is to be directly deducted and reported by the Social Bureau, the remaining donations will be collected by designated institutions of the Association, including the Central Bank, Bank of China, Bank of Communications, Shanghai Municipal Bank, Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank, etc., and the Shen Bao, Xinwen Bao, Shishi Xinbao, Min Bao, Shenzhou Daily, Zhonghua Daily, Shibao, and Dagong Bao newspapers. The Social Bureau has sent separate letters to various universities and circulated orders to all subordinate primary and secondary schools and institutions to comply accordingly.

Students Going to the United States During the Winter Vacation; Over Ten People Including Zhao Yuanlin; First Batch of Students Scheduled to Set Sail Tomorrow 114

The university system in the United States stipulates that new students are enrolled in two semesters each year. One is in the autumn, with classes beginning in mid-September. Therefore, most Chinese students going to study in the United States set sail in July or August. The spring semester starts in early February, so most students going to the United States depart in December or January. According to news from the Shanghai Global China Students Association, the students who plan to go to the United States for studies in the spring include Yuanlin, Fang Shengheng, Yang Dequan, Yu Hao, Huang Bingkun, Wang Guiwu, Xu Xuewu, and over ten others. These students have decided to sail on the Queen of Asia, which departs on the 25th of this month, the Asama Maru on January 9th, and the Empress of Canada, which departs on the 28th. It is said that the departure procedures for these students are being handled by the Global Student Association and will be completed soon.

In addition, the Study in England Guidance Association, affiliated with the Shanghai Study in England Students Association, recently sent separate letters to various universities, instructing students to transfer, as the winter vacation is approaching and there are not a few graduates from various universities who are going to England for further studies. If they want to understand the current situation of various universities in England and all the study abroad procedures, the Association will provide detailed guidance.

Chinese Members of the Shanghai Municipal Council Education Association Host Farewell Banquet for Chairman Sheppherd 115

Mr. Sheppherd, a British missionary in Shanghai, is over 70 years old and has lived in Shanghai for 30 years. He has served as the principal of Chinese and foreign schools and has been the Chairman of the Education Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Council for six years. He has decided to retire and return to his country. The Chinese members of the Education Association held a farewell banquet at the Banking Club in light of his impending departure. Attendees included the Western directors and Chinese directors of the Municipal Council, the director of the Chinese affairs, the secretary, the head of the Chinese Education Department, and the principals of Chinese primary and secondary schools, totaling over 50 people. Chairman Lin Kanghou delivered a farewell speech, stating that the development of Chinese education in the concession to what it is today is due to Mr. Sheppherd's efforts and promotion. His knowledge and morality are sufficient to be a model for us. On the occasion of his retirement and return to his country, we wish him longevity and boundless happiness. Mr. Sheppherd then delivered a response, followed by speeches by Liu Zhanen and Xi Yushu. The Chinese members of the Education Committee presented four pieces of Hunan embroidery as a gift. The principals of the Municipal Council's primary schools presented student achievements as a memento.

The New Globe Vocational School, New Globe Middle School, New Globe Second Primary School, and New Globe Primary School on Parker Road have been established for four years. The principals, brothers Zhang Xinbo and Zhang Zhonghuan, have worked diligently and arduously, resulting in rapid progress and an outstanding reputation for the schools. Children's Yearbook Published 117

The Shanghai Times Book Company's Children's Yearbook Society has commissioned Hu Zuyin, an expert in primary education, to edit the Children's Yearbook. This book, after a year of accumulation and the efforts of many people, has finally been compiled and printed. The cover features an inscription by Chen Heling, an expert in children's education. The book is rich in content, abundant in materials, emphasizes national defense knowledge, and introduces new scientific knowledge. It can be used as a current events teaching reader, a holiday homework reader, an extracurricular supplementary reader, a school and family prize, a Christmas and New Year gift, and a children's record book. One book serves six major purposes, making it a great creation among children's books and a must-read for modern children. Since its publication, it has been popular at home and abroad, with tens of thousands of copies sold. The book is currently on sale at a special price for one month. The paperback edition is on sale at half price, at 30 cents in national currency per copy. The hardcover edition is on sale at half price, at 40 cents in national currency per copy. The local agents are Wing On, Sincere, Sun Sun, The Sun and Four Great Companies, and the China National Goods Company, Shanghai Magazine Company. Metals　White Lead Wire: No New Stock Arrives, Sales Get Stronger… Inventories Become Thinner 122

White lead wire is a key sales item for the Changjiang (Yangtze River) and Ningbo merchant guilds. The annual export volume is very large. Recently, the price of new lead wire in Shanghai has risen sharply, causing those who usually use new lead wire to switch to white lead wire. As a result, sales of white lead wire have become increasingly brisk. Unfortunately, no new stock has arrived, and inventories are extremely low. Consequently, prices have also risen sharply. Yesterday, sizes 16 to 20 were quoted at 11 yuan per dan, an increase of 5 jiao from before. Transactions were heard to have been opened for as many as 400 to 500 dan, and negotiations were still underway for more than 600 dan. The briskness of the market is no less than that of other metal products.

Piece Goods: Approaching the End of the Year, Cotton Fabric Sales Are Universally Soft 125

Yesterday, fabric prices continued to fall. Although January futures rebounded by five yuan in the afternoon, it was difficult to reverse the downward trend. As the end of the year approaches, businesses are nearing closure, and money is becoming increasingly tight. As a result, fabric sales from all sources have become even more sluggish. Yesterday, sales prices for all goods were weak. Eastern fine cloth was particularly affected, with sluggish sales and weak demand. The market price fell most sharply, with each piece falling by twenty to thirty cents. For example, two-pound Dragon Head fine cloth, which had sold for a peak price of 9.80 yuan this month, is now nearing the critical point. The price drop for fine twill market cloth was slower, as factory supply was not strong and market demand was also slightly tight. Local factory fine cloth and fine twill also fell by varying amounts of twelve to thirty cents. Coarse twill and lightweight coarse cloth were able to maintain their prices due to a lack of stock. 14-pound, 16-pound, and 18-pound coarse cloth were weaker, with occasional price reductions of five to ten cents per piece. Colored cloth, direct tribute, broadcloth, flannel, and corduroy were unsustainable as inventories gradually increased, with prices falling several cents to four tenths of a yuan per piece, creating a very mixed market. Flannel saw the most dramatic drop, with 14-pound flannel falling from a high of 14 yuan to within 1-3 yuan, it is said.

Woolen Fabric Goods Becoming Increasingly Scarce 126

Yesterday, the woolen fabric market remained excellent. The stock of goods in Shanghai is becoming increasingly scarce, and buyer demand remains strong. Winter seasonal goods such as overcoating and riding breeches are very popular and in demand. Due to the current situation and the approaching end of the lunar year, sellers are generally unwilling to extend credit, so buyers are not adding large quantities. However, small-scale transactions are quite frequent. Inland merchants continue to send letters with purchase requests. Transactions from local shoe makers and men's and women's clothing makers are still numerous. However, due to the lack of stock, buyers are sighing in disappointment. Currently, riding breeches of the 20th grade, overcoating of the 5-6 yuan grade, Kemotecs, and horsehair sleeves are difficult to obtain even with immediate cash, it is said.

Grain: Sesame Plummets, Foreign Sesame Falls Less, Spot Raw Hemp Falls 80-90 Cents 127

Foreign sesame had risen sharply to 15 yuan. Since its peak, the market has been softening. After several days of silence, yesterday it finally moved. The Central Trust Bureau handled 600 tons of white sesame at a price of 14.60 yuan, a drop of 60 cents compared to the previous peak. Compared to the sharp drop in spot raw hemp, this is not as dramatic. Spot raw hemp plummeted by 80-90 cents. Yesterday, Shashi hemp opened at 11.50-11.60 yuan. Grain is sluggish because of the approaching lunar new year and the rainy and snowy conditions on the battlefront. All transactions are marked by wait-and-see attitude, so the market is particularly deserted. Total transactions in the city included more than 1,000 bags of various sesame seeds, 1,200 bags of various beans, 250 bags of black beans, more than 100 bags of mung beans, more than 100 bags of raw kernels, and 200 bags of peanuts, it is said.

Flour Industry Seeing Internal and External Divestments, Closing Accounts is Near... Market Value Too High 128

Yesterday's flour market saw a uniform decline across all months due to foreign wheat quotations falling 50 cents to 1.00 yuan in Chicago, 90 cents in Canada, and 2 pence in Liverpool. With foreign wheat falling sharply, rumors of improved European situation and sufficient Australian wheat stocks, and internally, the approaching end of accounting and high market values, speculators inside and outside the industry uniformly divested. The market fell continuously, with not only a significant downward trend, but also many large players exiting. As a result, all months fell sharply by six, seven, or eight cents. By the afternoon session, this month saw further divestments from long positions due to the approaching close, and the market fell another two or three cents. Distant months initially rose slightly due to long positions rolling over, but remained weak due to poor sentiment. If the Australian wheat situation eases, foreign wheat may continue to decline, making it difficult for the market to remain stable, it is said.

Australian Wheat Plummets, Wheat Futures Plummet by 20 Cents 129

Yesterday's wheat futures market saw a uniform and sharp decline across all months during the morning session. With foreign wheat quotations already falling sharply, and well-informed sources reporting that Italy and Austria were divesting wheat purchased in Australia, the situation favored short positions, resulting in a sudden surge in declines. This situation suggests that Australian wheat imports are inevitable, so trading was not very active at the opening, and prices plummeted. The current month did not open, but January fell by a significant 20 cents. February to April fell by 12 to 16 cents. By the afternoon session, the current month had opened, and the price had also fallen by 17 to 18 cents. Distant months saw some recovery due to floating covers, but overall sentiment was not as enthusiastic as the previous week. The spot wheat market saw factory demand holding back due to the sharp decline in standards, so no deliveries were seen, it is said.

Also, the Grain Exchange will be closed tomorrow (25th) in commemoration of the Yunnan Uprising. There will be a six-day market closure from the 20th of this month until January 4th of the 26th year. Trading will resume as usual on the 5th.

According to the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau's Raw Silk Group, the total export of raw silk from this port in the first half of December was 3,695 packages, which is not much different from the first half of November. The export of waste silk at 937 packages has been reduced. This period's raw silk was shipped 1,895 packages to Europe, 1,387 packages to Europe, 299 packages to India, and 114 packages to other countries. The export of white factory warp silk during this period was 2,986 packages, which was not very exciting, but the export of warp silk was stronger than other months, reaching 190 packages. Newly Appointed Judge of the International Court of Justice Zheng Tianxi Departed for His Post Yesterday, Mayor Wu and Others Welcomed Him at the Port, Said to Lament the Xi'an Incident Upon Departure 140

Dr. Zheng Tianxi, the newly appointed Chinese judge to the International Court of Justice, originally planned to depart for his post at the beginning of next year after being elected. However, due to an urgent telegram from the International Court of Justice, he advanced his departure to yesterday afternoon at 3:00 p.m., accompanying his wife and children, a total of four people, on the German postal ship "Hoxter" to The Hague.

Sending Off Party

The ship was originally docked on the river surface at pontoons No. 11 and No. 12. Zheng and his wife boarded the ship at the new customs pier at 1:30 p.m. Wu Tiecheng, Mayor of Shanghai Municipality, Yu Hongjun, Secretary-General of the Municipal Government, Wu Zixiang, Director of the Municipal Treasury, Zheng Lai, Director of the Customs Administration of the Ministry of Finance, Yang Peng, President of the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, Qiao Wanxuan, Chief Prosecutor, Guo Yun Guan, President of the First Special Court, Xiang Zhejuan, Chief Prosecutor, Cha Liangjian, Chief Secretary, and more than 20 of Zheng's relatives and friends went to the ship to welcome him. Zheng had arrived in Shanghai from Beijing on the 21st to wait for the ship. Mayor Wu had hosted a banquet for him the night before to see him off.

Remarks Before Departure

Before departing, Zheng told reporters from the Xinsheng News Agency that the International Court of Justice is scheduled to hold its annual meeting on February 1 next year, which is the official start of the annual court term. Because I followed the urging telegram, I specifically advanced my departure so that I could arrive before the term. I plan to take office on the same day. The term of the International Court of Justice judge is nine years. I am filling the vacancy left by Mr. Wang Liangchou, and there are still three years and ten months remaining. At that time, the terms of all judges will expire and they must all be re-elected. I will still be a candidate. Zheng then spoke about the Xi'an Incident with great indignation, saying that foreigners used to ridicule our country as a heap of loose sand. Since the realization of unification in recent months, they have looked at us with different eyes, and our international status has increased a lot. Unexpectedly, the Xi'an Incident suddenly occurred, which is very painful. For the sake of our country's future, we deeply hope that Chairman Chiang Kai-shek will regain his freedom as soon as possible and turn danger into safety. Otherwise, the international perception that has just improved will inevitably change again.

Participation in the Paris Exposition: Product Collection Committee Established Yesterday; Notice of Product Collection Rules 141

The China Participation in the Paris International Exposition Product Collection Committee held its inaugural meeting at the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM. Dozens of people attended, including Li Shizeng, Chu Minyi, Pan Gongzhan, Wang Xiaolai, Lin Kanghou, Guo Bingwen, Zhao Jinqing, Xie Zhongfu, Zhao Zhiyou, Liu Xichang, Wang Jiean, Xie Xiaochu, Jin Runxiang, Yan Esheng, and Zhou Bangjun. The meeting was chaired by Chief Representative Chu Minyi, with Tian Shouchang as secretary. First, the chairman reported on the progress of preparations for participating in the Paris Exposition and spoke on the significant importance of participating. Next, Li Shizeng reported on the reasons for initiating the organization for participating in the Exposition, stating briefly: The scope of the Exposition is very broad, encompassing both cultural and economic categories. Motivated by the World Cultural Cooperation French Association, they strongly urged China to participate. I, along with Mr. Wu Zhihui, are managing the World Cultural Cooperation Chinese Association, hence its initiation of participation, along with the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, the Bankers' Association, and leaders from various sectors, to jointly organize the China Participation in the Paris Modern Arts and Technology International Exposition Association to prepare exhibits and participate in the competition. The hope is to achieve great results with minimal expenditure, and so on. Next, the presidium was elected, and as a result, Li Shizeng, Chu Minyi, Wang Xiaolai, Lin Kanghou, and Pan Gongzhan were elected as the presidium. Next, the rules for collecting items were discussed, and it was resolved to pass the original text and additionally appoint Hu Xiyuan, Xiang Kangyuan, Wang Zhixin, Pan Yangyao, Shen Hengyi, and Xu Shiqi as members of the Product Collection Committee. The speeches of the representatives and the product collection rules are recorded below:

Chu's Report

Chief Representative Chu Minyi reported, "Ladies and gentlemen, today we are holding the inaugural meeting of the China Participation in the Paris Exposition Product Collection Committee. I am deeply honored by your presence. Regarding the progress of participating in the Paris Exposition, I would like to report in detail. The French government has scheduled the Modern Arts and Technology International Exposition Association to be held in Paris on May 1st next year. All countries in the world have been invited to participate. Of course, our country is also on the list of invitees. However, the government had previously declined for various reasons. Subsequently, the World Cultural Cooperation French Association repeatedly requested China's participation, citing the extremely close and harmonious relations between China and France, with many cooperative ventures in culture. In particular, in industry and technology, there is a need for mutual contact and cooperation. Therefore, they strongly urge China to participate. At the same time, French Ambassador Naggiar came to China and spoke on this matter, believing that although the government had declined, it would be acceptable for social organizations to initiate an organization to participate. Therefore, Li Shizeng, Wu Zhihui, Cai Yuanpei, Zhang Jingjiang, and Minyi and others from the World Cultural Cooperation Chinese Association initiated and convened leaders from the cultural, educational, industrial, and commercial sectors, including Wang Xiaolai, Du Yuesheng, Lin Kanghou, Zhang Xiaolin, Qian Xinzhi, and others, and after several meetings at the World Society, everyone recognized that this matter is very important. Because Paris is a district where world cultures converge, and this grand exposition is being held, people from various countries will certainly go to visit. Now that all countries have participated, if China alone does not go, it will have implications for its international standing. Moreover, in recent years, China's various construction undertakings in culture, education, and industrial and commercial enterprises have made considerable progress, and we can take this opportunity to engage in international promotion, so that people from various countries understand the situation of the emerging China. Therefore, it was resolved that the World Cultural Cooperation Chinese Association, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, and the Bankers' Association, four groups, and leaders from the cultural, educational, industrial, and commercial sectors, would jointly organize the 'China Participation in the Paris International Exposition Association,' and elected Chu Minyi, Zhao Zhiyou, Liu Fucheng, Xie Dongfa, and Liu Xichang as representatives to form a delegation to bring cultural, educational, industrial, and commercial exhibits to France to participate, with Minyi as the chief representative, responsible for preparing everything. The organization charter and detailed rules of the delegation's office were approved. The delegation's office was established and started operating on the 15th of this month. Regarding the collection of items, we must gather the strength of the whole country to select excellent exhibits in order to win glory for the country. Because this association is international in nature and is located in Paris, the largest and most prosperous city in the world, it is truly related to the national image and must be done with utmost dedication. Therefore, following the example of participating in the Belgian Centennial Independence Exposition in 1930, we organized the Product Collection Committee and appointed you all as Product Collection Committee members. You are all leaders in the cultural, industrial, and commercial sectors and must have great wisdom and scholarship for our reference. Therefore, today we ask you to carefully discuss it, and we hope that you will not hesitate to give your advice. After holding the inaugural meeting of the Product Collection Committee today, we will begin to collect items. We urge everyone to enthusiastically help and select exquisite items for the competition. However, one thing I would like to ask you to pay attention to is to focus on the quality of the items, not the quantity. In other words, the items are not about quantity, but about quality. I feel that the financial abundance and economic strength of a country are entirely dependent on its trade surplus and trade deficit. Therefore, internally, we must promote domestic goods, and externally, we must especially promote international trade. All of you present are leaders in the industrial and commercial sectors and have certainly already understood this principle. China has had many emerging industries in recent years. How should we promote international trade? I believe that this is an excellent opportunity. We must do our best to promote it externally, so that foreigners understand the extent to which our domestic goods have progressed in recent years and adopt them accordingly. Because various domestic goods are transported to the exposition for display, foreigners will see that China has items that foreign countries do not have, or are inferior to. Then they will know that buying our goods will increase international trade. Therefore, participating in international expositions is not only related to the national image, but is actually of great benefit to promoting domestic goods and developing industrial and commercial enterprises. I have managed expositions several times, including the last one, such as participating in the Belgian Centennial Independence Exposition in 1930, and the awards we received ranked third among all countries. Although not a perfect achievement, we still won international honor. In particular, we provided special protection to the exhibits of all sectors, such as round-trip insurance and venue insurance. We spared no effort in doing what should be done. Therefore, the exhibitors at that exposition all received awards and benefits. After the exhibits were sold at the venue, the sale price was returned, otherwise the original items were returned. Therefore, the exhibitors did not suffer any loss. This time, we will still follow the past experience and do it more seriously. As the chief representative, I will take full responsibility. All the necessary safety measures for transporting items and displaying them at the venue will be adopted as much as possible. I dare to predict to you that, like last time, after returning home from participating in the Paris Exposition, all the exhibitors' items will definitely not suffer the slightest loss. For various items, if they belong to those that are sold, the sale price will be returned after the sale. For those that are non-saleable or have not been sold, they will be returned to the original owner together after the closing of the exposition. Please convey this meaning to all manufacturers and industrialists. I will definitely take full responsibility. But what I would like to ask you to pay attention to is that time is very pressing and we must step up the collection. Because the conference opens on May 1st, our group's exhibits must be packed and shipped out in March. There are only two months of preparation time. Therefore, I would like to ask you to help especially. I hope that our country's international status can be increased as a result, and everything can achieve good results. Not only will I personally be grateful, but the country's future will also benefit from it.

Product Collection Rules

China Participation in the Paris International Exposition Association Delegation Office Product Collection Rules (A) Cultural, Educational, and Artistic Exhibits. Article 1: The collection of cultural, educational, and artistic exhibits is limited to those related to culture, education, science, and art. Exhibitors are limited to those with Republic of China nationality. Article 2: All cultural institutions, scientific organizations, specialized schools above the junior college level, vocational schools, and individuals with excellent exhibits of special value may send them to the conference for participation. Article 3: The scope of collection is limited to the following categories: Category 1: Educational Administration: (1) Work reports or commemorative publications of specialized schools above the junior college level and social education institutions, and publications of a similar nature (mainly those that are bound into volumes, visually appealing, and systematically compiled; both Chinese and Western languages are acceptable). (2) Explanatory documents on the current academic system and educational system. (3) Various statistical tables, classification tables, or summary tables on educational administration (such as the number of schools, number of students, number of staff, funding organization, staffing, etc. in each province). (4) Architectural photos, drawings, models, and explanatory documents of school buildings and various social education institutions. Category 2: Educational Books and Ironware Specimens: (5) Various teaching materials, textbooks, and excellent extracurricular reading materials. (6) Ancient books and rare editions related to China's education and culture. (7) Monographs discussing modern education. (8) Systematic teaching designs and reports on their results. (9) Various models and charts self-made by vocational schools and specialized schools above the junior college level. (10) Educational supplies and instruments invented or finely crafted in the country. Category 3: Works of Art: (11) Modern famous books. (12) Excellent sculptures. (13) Embroidery and textiles. (14) Lacquerware, bronzes, and porcelain. (15) Handicrafts and other works with artistic value. (16) Excellent ancient and modern musical instruments, scores, and records. (17) Beautiful ancient costumes, dance, drama costumes, supplies, and photos with explanatory documents. (18) Scenic photos from various places. Category 4: Research Achievements and Sports: (19) Performance items by students of various vocational schools. (20) Excellent graduation theses and performance items from various universities. (21) The latest scientific inventions and writings by experts, activity performance photos of boy scouts, performance photos of military training and troop exercises, and various sports and physical education photos. Article 4: Because the collection period is urgent, only the above items are listed. If there are excellent exhibits that are indeed of display value and are not included in the above items, they may still be selected and sent. (B) Industrial, Commercial, and Technological Exhibits. Article 5: The collection of industrial, commercial, and technological exhibits is limited to domestic goods. Exhibitors are limited to those with Republic of China nationality. Article 6: All companies, factories, or individuals who can manufacture large quantities of goods and promote them overseas may send them to the conference for participation. However, the following excellent items must be selected: (1) Silk fabrics: Various silk fabrics, Shandong silk (choose the exquisite ones), Nanjing silk and satin (for foreign decorative items, choose those with improved weaving methods, such as Zhang velvet, etc. Silk fabric figure and landscape paintings. (2) Embroidered items: Various Gu embroidery and Xiang embroidery, curtains, embroidered door curtains, window curtains, etc. are preferred, must be suitable for foreign doors and windows, embroidered cushions and embroidered bags, the above is better if they can be inlaid with Chinese official patches, the color is not limited, women's shawls, those with bright colors and heavy status are preferred, but black ones should not be too many, because foreigners use black for mourning, clothing table cloths, screen velvet flowers, must be manufactured exquisitely, suitable for foreigners. (3) Knitted and wool items: Lace, wide and narrow are suitable, the color is not limited, straw hat edges and hair nets, must be made of fine materials, carpets, plain and bright are acceptable, the size is up to each participant. (4) Kiln-fired items: Cloisonné enamel (fine and delicate is valued), enamel (suitable for women's decoration), porcelain, enamelware, pottery (beautiful texture, well-made, beautiful form, suitable for foreigners. (5) Leather goods: Sable, fox, gray squirrel, otter, rabbit skin, slender-haired white lambskin, various leather goods (must be light, warm, and suitable for foreign women to make coats), those that can make scarves are also suitable to choose the best ones. (6) Tea: Tea leaves, black tea (suitable for foreign tastes), green tea (choose the best ones). (7) Carvings and statues: Ivory carvings, wood and stone carvings and statues (exquisite and delicate are valued). (8) Metal utensils: Teapots, vases, pots, bowls, cups, saucers, etc. (these must be skillfully handcrafted and suitable for foreigners. (9) Decorations: Feather fans, tortoiseshell, coral, jadeite, glasswork, jade, autumn horns, and objects inlaid with gold, silver, and precious stones. (10) Raw materials: Raw silk, hemp, cotton, gallnuts. (11) Other items: Drawnwork glass gauze, fans, marble, mahogany images, silver carvings, products from Beijing and Fujian, lacquerware, crystal, agate, Hangzhou paper umbrellas. In addition, if there are exquisite items that can be sold overseas or are sufficient to express national essence and increase national glory, even if they do not belong to the above categories, they may also be sent. Article 7: The items to be collected must have one of the following elements: (1) Currently international trade goods and those that may become international trade goods in the future. (2) Those that are widely promoted in domestic commercial ports. (3) Exquisite and useful, recognized as having the value of exhibits. Article 8: The following items are not included in the collection: (1) Those that are dangerous and may damage other items. (2) Those that are harmful to customs, order, and hygiene. (3) Those that are considered to have no value as exhibits. (4) Those that are foreign goods that have been repackaged. Article 9: The quantity of each type of item to be collected shall not be excessive. Article 10: All items to be collected must be affixed with labels, with the following indicated above: (1) Name of the item. (2) Name of the exhibiting institution or individual. (3) The category and item to which the exhibit belongs. (4) Indicate the value. (5) If it is a non-sale item, indicate the words "non-sale item". Article 11: All exhibits to be collected shall be submitted by the exhibitor with an application and a list of exhibits to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce for clear delivery, and a receipt shall be signed and issued by this office. After the end of the exhibition in France, the items shall be returned based on the receipt, and the original price shall be returned for those that have been sold. Article 12: This delegation will compile a general catalog of Chinese goods, bound into volumes. For publicity purposes, exhibitors may provide a detailed description of the history, capital, business status, types of exhibits of the company or store, and whether they have won awards at international expositions (if they have won awards, what kind of awards they were). A four-inch photograph can be taken and explained in detail in Western or Chinese languages for inclusion in the catalog and distribution at the venue. Article 13: Item numbers will be handled by the office of this delegation. Article 14: If an exhibitor has a large number of items to be collected and voluntarily produces a separate catalog for distribution at the venue for publicity purposes, the office of this delegation can also distribute it on their behalf. Article 15: This office will not accept any exhibits that are damaged or incomplete. Otherwise, it will be responsible for protection (such as venue insurance and round-trip transportation insurance), but it will not be liable for damages that cannot be prevented by human force. Article 16: All exhibits to be collected must be reviewed and inspected before they can be transported to France for competition (the regulations of the review committee will be determined separately). Article 17: All exhibits to be collected should be listed on a separate catalog, indicating which category the exhibit belongs to. Article 18: The deadline for collecting exhibits at the office of this delegation is March 1, 1937.
