Su Gongwang Discusses the Production and Sale of Gas Masks: Private National Defense Industry Should Be Supported and Cherished, But Must Be Controlled to Avoid Various Abuses 145

The Air Defense Association has been publishing notices in various newspapers in this city in recent days, warning citizens to pay attention to selecting and purchasing gas masks. A reporter from the Central News Agency yesterday interviewed Su Gongwang, the Secretary-General of the Association, who stated the following:

According to Mr. Su

Gas masks are originally useful tools for defending against the enemy's use of poison gas during air raids. Therefore, manufacturers must strive for excellent quality of materials and pay particular attention to technology, so that the products manufactured can indeed defend against poison gas during air raids and not cause mistakes. However, it has been found that the gas masks currently manufactured in our country, in addition to those supervised by the government authorities, also include quite a few that are automatically manufactured and sold by other manufacturers. It is not known whether they can meet the requirements of defending against poison gas, because they have never been controlled or inspected. If the effectiveness of use is considered, there is really no certainty. If this kind of bad phenomenon is allowed to continue to spread, the danger to the future of poison gas prevention will be even more unimaginable.

Our Association is Responsible

for promoting air defense in Shanghai, and poison gas prevention is one aspect of air defense tasks. Seeing such a bad phenomenon occurring in the manufacture and sale of gas masks, if we remain silent, we will feel that we have failed in our mission. Therefore, in recent days, in addition to submitting a request to the municipal government, which forwarded it to the Ministry of Military Affairs, to quickly devise effective measures to ban it, we have also published notices in the newspapers to awaken people's attention, hoping that when purchasing gas masks, they will make careful and meticulous selections, so as to avoid wasting money now and not obtaining safety guarantees in the future. We also hope that if people encounter difficulties, they can come to our Association for inquiries, and we will sincerely provide detailed instructions. Furthermore, our Association has

Several Opinions on Gas Masks, which we plan to suggest to the Central Government for adoption. For example, gas masks currently manufactured in our country under the supervision of government authorities cost about twelve yuan per set, which is still a bit expensive. It is best to find ways to reduce costs within the possible range and sell them at low prices, so that people will be happy to buy them and easily equip themselves. In this way, both purchasing power can be increased and popularization among the people can be achieved, which will make it easier to enhance the nation's and society's ability to prevent poison gas, and the relationship is very close. Also, it has been found that

There are Many Kinds of Poison Gas, which are known to the world, including lachrymatory, asphyxiating, vesicant, sneezing, and toxic, among others. These were all invented around 1914 and were used during the World War. Although we must guard against them, scientific progress in the world is rapid. It has been twenty years since the European War, so progress in poison gas research is inevitable. Moreover, in the current stage, countries are competing to replenish their military equipment and improve their weapons, and they must have made new inventions in the manufacture of poison gas. However, because of military secrets, it is impossible to know. However, for the sake of prevention, we must pay serious attention to it and improve the defense weapons, such as gas masks, as much as possible, striving for perfection, so as to be able to cope with it. In short, the current world can be said to be a

Scientific World. Everything new and progressive has been baptized by science. We must do things according to scientific methods in order to be reasonable. The issue of gas masks is no exception. Therefore, in terms of manufacturing, we must apply scientific methods, vigorously research, and catch up to meet practical needs. In terms of promotion, we must also apply scientific methods, first conducting investigations, statistics, and overall planning, and properly allocating them to achieve popularization. For manufacturers who automatically manufacture, on the one hand, we should cherish them to foster the development of private national defense industries, and on the other hand, we should control them and conduct strict inspections to prevent unscrupulous merchants from imitating and manufacturing crudely, wasting people's wealth without helping practical use. However, this matter is of great importance and should be given close attention by the government authorities, who should advocate and supervise it and formulate an overall plan to facilitate progress. Mr. Su also said that this matter is very important to the future of the nation and society, and he sincerely hopes that the press will provide more assistance and widely promote and guide it.

Jiangsu Province and Shanghai Authorities Repairing the Jiangnan Seawall: Work Has Already Started Within the City Area; Work Within the Provincial Area Is Scheduled to Begin on Time 148

The Jiangnan Seawall project is of great importance to the safety of residents in the coastal counties of Jiangnan. Therefore, the government authorities are sparing no effort to repair the seawall. The Gaoqiao Seawall within the scope of this city is currently being repaired by the Municipal Bureau of Public Works in conjunction with the Labor Service Committee. Because the seawall is relatively short, it can be completed in a short period of time. The seawall within the Jiangsu Province is more than 30,000 zhang long. The seawall in Shishan and Songjiang is more prone to damage due to the large tides, so repairs are even more urgent. This time, the Jiangsu Provincial Government, despite the scarcity of funds, has raised funds for the sake of the safety of residents in dozens of counties in Jiangnan and decided to start a large-scale repair project on March 1 next year. It is estimated that the Longjiang Temple, Jinshan Mouth, and Toutumiao sections of Songjiang need 4,233 cubic meters of stone and 1,627 wooden piles; the Shidong and Chuchengjing sections of Baoshan need 913 cubic meters of stone and 442 wooden piles; the Daotangmiao section of Taicang needs 1,822 cubic meters of stone and 1,082 wooden piles; and the Xuliujingkou section of Changshu needs 3,445 cubic meters of stone and 2,821 wooden piles. The stone used is all Xueshan stone from Songjiang, and the wood is Jian wood, which is durable. Currently, the transportation of stones is a major project, so the Gongxing Company, which is responsible for the stones, has begun transportation. It is expected that the project will be completed in the summer of next year.

First Snow in This City 155

The climate in this city warmed up once last week, but has gradually become colder in recent days. As a result, prices of vegetables and other items have soared, and all kinds of diseases have also multiplied due to the dry weather, especially throat diseases. Since yesterday morning, the climate has changed again, with the cold wind piercing to the bone and a gloomy and unclouded atmosphere. At about ten o'clock, it started to rain lightly, but it was intermittent. At noon, it changed to snow pellets, but stopped soon, and the drizzle continued to fall. At about 2:10 in the afternoon, it changed to snow again, sparse but not dense. At about four o'clock, it gradually became smooth and dense, like goose feathers falling from the sky. The rain stopped, so there was gradually snow accumulation between the roofs. At about seven o'clock in the afternoon, looking from a high place, the whole city was already silvery white, and the snow was still not slowing down. It only stopped snowing at about eleven o'clock. The general farmers, after this timely snow, were all beaming with joy, and all kinds of miscellaneous diseases will also be reduced as a result. However, the market price of vegetables will still be difficult to stabilize.

Discovered in Xinmin Road: A Large Quantity of Obscene Books, Totaling Over Four Thousand Volumes; Two Men and Women Arrested 156

Yesterday afternoon around three o'clock, Wu Songshan, a detective from the Sixth Squad of the Municipal Public Security Bureau's Detective Corps, acting on a tip, learned that a large quantity of obscene books were being bound at No. 6 Dexing Lane, Xinmin Road, Zhabei. The detective immediately reported to squad leader Qian Tianxiong, who dispatched team leader Liu Bingyuan and detective Chen Mingsheng. Together with the Xinzha Branch Bureau, Wang, the bureau chief, sent Officer Wu Dichen, who was on duty, to the address. They found Yu Zichun, who was binding the books. Over ten large bundles of obscene books were seized. Along with the witness, he was taken to the team. During interrogation, Yu Zichun, 54 years old and from Zhenjiang, confessed that he made a living by binding books for others. Three or four days ago, an old woman named Chen Zhu came and said she had a large number of small books she wanted him to bind. She brought the books to his place, and he had been hiring workers to bind them for the past two days. They had already been completed but had not yet been sent out when he was arrested and brought to the case. Chen Zhu lived at No. 19 Nanxing Road, according to him. After verifying the confession, the team immediately sent officers to Nanxing Road and brought Chen Zhu in for questioning. Chen Zhu confessed that she was 51 years old, from Wuxi, and her late husband was named Chen Baisan, who had passed away more than twenty years ago. She could not make a living in Wuxi, so she came to Shanghai more than ten years ago and lived in the British Concession, at the corner of a sack, weaving cloth for a living. Later, she became acquainted with a book stall vendor from Suzhou named Chen Aqing and lived with him at No. 19 Nanxing Road for more than ten years. Her lover, Chen Aqing, also passed away last year. Currently, because she had no one to rely on, she entrusted someone to bind the many loose copies left by her late husband, intending to sell them and use the money to repay his debts. She claimed that she did not know the content of the books and was unaware that she was violating the law. After verifying the confession, the team immediately escorted her and the witness to the Xinzha Branch Bureau for disposal. The obscene books seized included "The Latest Japanese Social Romantic Photos," "Secret Records of a Licentious Country," "An Overview of Sexual Intercourse," "Special Issue on Sexual History," "Taste of Sex," "The Sexual World: School Principal and Teachers Gang Rape Female Students," "Ten Thousand Yuan Exclusively Occupies the Sisters: Civilization Sticking Hanji," "Specializing in Eating Young Men," "One Boat, Double Oars," "Female Grind," "Secret Records of the Bridal Chamber," "Tongue Battle Confuses the Cave," "Flesh Monk," "Tianjin Male Prostitute," "Secrets of Girls' School," "Pockmarked Sixth Miss," "Dangling Arm Technique," "Strange, So Strange," "One Look and Your Heart Moves, Can Be Called the Ancestor of Thieves," etc. The words were quite filthy and difficult to read to the end.

Wusong Ward Corner: Expanding Shoal, Digging a Small River; The Junchu Bureau's Haihu Dredger Completes Over a Year of Work 157

The shoal along the ward corner of the Pudong Municipal Ward, across from Zhou Tang at the Wusong Yunzao Creek estuary, was quite wide and protruded significantly into the river surface, making it inconvenient for boats and sails to enter and exit. Moreover, the area was on the main route to and from a point of importance, and was also at a bend (its shape resembling the Lujiazui of this city). Therefore, incidents of ships colliding and damage, as well as dangers of capsizing, occurred from time to time. The Engineering Department of the Junchu Bureau, in view of the risks, ordered the large dredger "Haihu" to dig a small river in the middle of the shoal, so that sailboats within the capacity of one thousand dan (a unit of weight) could enter and exit from the small river, while larger steamers could navigate in the main river. This would not only facilitate merchants but also reduce the various dangers of collisions. The small river was more than a thousand feet long, with the widest part of the river surface being three hundred feet, the narrowest two hundred feet, and an average of two hundred and fifty feet. The river was eight feet deep. The "Haihu" dredger had been digging for more than a year, and the project has now been completed. Yesterday, according to Li Ahong, the owner of the "Haihu" ship, although the two ends of the small river have now been opened up, the area is a shifting sandy beach, subject to constant rising. The engineering design specified a depth of eight feet, but the rising is quite rapid. Therefore, ships with deeper drafts should pay attention when navigating in the area.

Gao Qifeng's Coffin Moved: Public Memorial Held Today; Wang Jingwei Personally Selected Tomb Inscription 158

Revolutionary pioneer Mr. Gao Qifeng passed away on November 2nd of the 22nd year of the Republic. The Central Political Committee, chaired by Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Beijing Mayor Ma Chaojun, Chu Minyi, Ye Gongchuo, Zhang Ji, Gu Zhenggang, Wang Shijie, He Xiangning, and others, specifically initiated a public funeral, scheduled for 3:00 PM today at the Chinese Funeral Home on Haig Road. The coffin will be moved at 4:00 PM, and the funeral procession will begin at 6:00 PM. On the 27th, he will be buried at Qixia Mountain in Nanjing. The preparatory committee published Mr. Gao's biography, stating: "On November 2nd of the 22nd year of the Republic, Mr. Gao Qifeng of Panyu passed away at the Dahua Hospital in Shanghai. Alas, with the decline of our nation's art, we have now lost this guide. This is not just a private sorrow. Mr. Gao, whose given name was Rong, was known by his courtesy name. He was orphaned at a young age, determined to study diligently. At the age of thirteen, he traveled to Japan, specializing in art, especially fond of painting. He met with Mr. Sun Yat-sen during his travels to Japan and secretly planned. He often kept a secret room full of bombs, and Mr. Gao slept on top of them for several days and nights, which awed his colleagues. After the Republic was established, Mr. Gao remained aloof from worldly affairs, not asking about politics, and devoted himself to painting. He and his colleagues ran an aesthetics library and produced photographic magazines, supporting themselves. Mr. Sun Yat-sen often praised him, saying that his diligence was unparalleled. Mr. Gao's painting skills further advanced. His paintings of landscapes, figures, birds, beasts, insects, and fish drew from various schools, integrating Chinese and foreign styles, capturing the essence of the divine, and opening up new perspectives. Knowledgeable people all praised him. Qiu Canghai presented him with a poem, saying, 'Returning from across the sea, China is about to change; with a stroke of the brush, he creates wondrous things,' which is a true record. In the 7th year of the Republic, he returned to teach and lecture, with as many as several thousand students following him. He had many outstanding disciples. In the 14th year of the Republic, Lingnan University hired him as a professor of aesthetics, and also gifted land to build a residence, which was unprecedented. The following year, the National Government built the Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall in Guangzhou, with grand regulations. They asked Mr. Gao to use his paintings of sea eagles, white horses, and lions as decorations, paying him handsomely from the national treasury. All three had been praised by Mr. Sun Yat-sen, who considered them representative of the revolutionary spirit and possessing the beauty of the new era. Mr. Gao did not engage in production, nor did he seek fame. He solely devoted himself to painting and taught tirelessly. His health was weak and he was prone to illness, but he did not rest. Among his students, only Zhang Kunyi took on the role of nurse, attending to him with meticulous care, allowing Mr. Gao to focus on his painting. Mr. Gao then adopted her as his daughter. This autumn, at the Sino-German Art Exhibition, Mr. Gao was chosen to represent China and go to Germany. Mr. Gao happily arrived in Shanghai to discuss matters. On the 16th and 17th of the month, he fell ill. Doctors said that he had a cold and overexertion, triggered a lung disease. After weeks of diagnosis and treatment, it was ineffective, and he passed away. During his illness, his mind was still clear. He first telegraphed Zhao Ming and others, requesting that the Tianfeng Building where he lived be used as the Qifeng Painting Academy, forever for the use of those who completed the art specialty. His lifetime works were distributed to art galleries at home and abroad. He also ordered that the debts owed by friends and relatives be canceled, not seeking repayment. Alas, this is enough to see his integrity. Mr. Gao passed away at the young age of forty-five. If he had been given more years, his contribution to the future of our country's art would have been even greater. Now it has ended here, which is not just a loss for the Gao family. Mr. Gao was erudite and versatile. In addition to painting, he was also skilled in poetry. His published works include 'The Truth Pictorial,' 'Qifeng Painting Collection,' 'New Painting Studies,' 'Qifeng Painting Models,' 'Art History,' 'Aesthetics and Education,' 'Origins of Aesthetics,' and other books. His works have been exhibited at the Ministry of Education, the National Art Exhibition, the Sino-Japanese Painting Exhibition, the West Lake Exposition, the Italian Panama World Exposition, the Belgian Centennial Exposition, and the Paris Art Exhibition, all of which received the highest awards. His colleagues will compile and publish his lifetime masterpieces. Central Political Committee Chairman Jin Jing Shushu, due to Mr. Gao's public funeral in Beijing, personally wrote the tomb inscription and sent it to Shanghai, praising him to the utmost. The text is long and will not be recorded here."

Zhabei Public Bus Employees Go on Strike Yesterday Morning; Party and Government Agencies Persuade Them to Resume Work at 11:00 AM 162

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, the entire staff of the Zhabei Chinese Public Bus Company demanded that year-end double pay be issued according to the annual precedent. After the union negotiated with the company to no avail, they went on strike yesterday morning. Fortunately, after party and government agencies sent personnel to persuade them, they fully resumed work at 11:40 AM. Details are as follows:

Strike Yesterday Morning

Regarding the year-end double pay, after the Sixth District Public Bus Industry Union negotiated with the Zhabei Chinese Public Bus Company to no avail, starting yesterday morning, Zhabei public buses on Route 1 (North Station to Jiangwan), Route 3 (North Station to Zhenru), Route 4 (North Station to the Municipal Government), Route 5 (North Station to the Municipal Government Dormitory), and Route 6 (Liping Road to the Water and Electricity Company) operated as usual, but all ticket sellers refused to sell tickets.

Party and Government Persuasion

The Social Bureau, after receiving the report at 9:00 AM yesterday, immediately sent Ren Zhusun, a mediator from the Third Section, to investigate the truth and persuade the workers to resume work first and wait for legal mediation. At the same time, Zhu Xuefan, chairman of the General Labor Union, after receiving a request from the workers, personally went to the company to find a way to mediate and persuade the workers to resume work. The workers accepted the persuasion from the government and others, and from 11:40 AM, all of them resumed work, and public buses on all routes resumed selling tickets.

Mediation Today

In order to quickly resolve the matter, the Social Bureau has scheduled a mediation meeting at 2:00 PM today, convening the Sixth District Public Bus Industry Professional Guild and the Zhabei Public Bus Company at the Bureau's First Mediation Room in the city center. The notice has been sent out last night.

Company Submission

The Chinese Public Bus Company submitted a document to the Social Bureau, stating: "Submission for the matter of a petition. Our company humbly shoulders the responsibility of public transportation in the urban area, enduring hardship and persevering for several years. However, business has been repeatedly affected by the current situation, and financial resources are extremely strained. In addition, in order to follow the needs of the new urban area's transportation, the routes have been expanded, and the number of kilometers driven has increased accordingly. Therefore, based on the past eleven months of operation this year, not only can dividends not be distributed according to regulations, but also the income and expenditure comparison shows a loss of more than ten thousand yuan. Unexpectedly, on the 8th of this month, we received a letter from the Sixth District Public Bus Industry Union stating that the year-end bonus for all employees this year should be issued based on 25 days. If we follow the request, it will cost more than six thousand yuan in national currency to cover the payment. However, our company suffered a severe loss of half of its capital during the January 28th Incident, and this amount has not been compensated to this day. Since resuming operations after the war, statistics over the years have still shown losses, which means that the losses this year are even greater. If we add the additional burden of the year-end bonus, the company will not be able to cope. We have answered the union and asked for their understanding. Later, on the 17th and 21st of this month, union directors Mao Xinhui, Liu Shouchun, Liang Guoming, Quan Renzhong, and Zhou Yimin came to discuss the matter twice. However, although the directors knew the company's difficulties and claimed that they had repeatedly explained to the workers, some of them still did not agree. In order to find a solution, it was decided at the time that each party would submit to your bureau for mediation, so as to seek a fair judgment and quell the dispute. Now, we respectfully submit a document with a statement of the company's operation for the past eleven months of this year for your examination. In order to avoid disputes, we also ask your bureau to convene the Sixth District Public Bus Industry Union for mediation as soon as possible, so as to maintain business and benefit transportation, which is truly a public convenience. Furthermore, Article 45, Paragraph 3 of the company's articles of association states that if there is a surplus in the year, 10% of the employees' bonus will be allocated, which shows that the company has long taken into account the welfare of employees. Combined statements. Respectfully submitted to the Director of the Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau, Pan.

Company Overview

According to sources from the company, it opened in November of the 17th year of the Republic, with a capital of 100,000 yuan. Ninety-five percent of the shareholders are overseas Chinese from the Americas. After the January 28th Incident, there was a deficit of 50,000 yuan. It was not until the 23rd year that the full amount was replenished. In order to meet the needs of urban prosperity, it was decided to increase the capital by another 100,000 yuan. When operations resumed after the war, most of the vehicles were damaged and incomplete. Three vehicles were dismantled, pieced together, and refurbished first and put into service. Subsequently, repairs and additions were gradually made, and today there are 45 vehicles. At that time, the number of employees started at 99, and now it has increased to 244. The annual salary started at more than 23,000 yuan, and now it has increased to more than 112,000 yuan. Since the old shareholders invested, in addition to the 100 yuan stock being changed to 50 yuan, dividends were only paid once in the 19th year, and so far they have not been able to be paid according to the regulations. Also, based on the past eleven months of operation this year, the income and expenditure comparison, excluding dividends, shows a loss of 12,000 yuan.

During the Shaanxi Incident, the Eurasia Company:

Revised Flight Routes 163

According to the Central News Agency, the outbreak of the Xi'an Incident first affected transportation between Shanghai and Shaanxi, causing the Shaanxi-Lanzhou section of the Eurasia Aviation Company's Shanghai-Shaanxi line and the Lanzhou-Baotou line to be blocked and unable to fly. The company has now changed its flight schedule during this period so that, except for the Lanzhou and Shaanxi stations, all other stations can still connect with Beijing, Shanghai, Pingzhen, and other stations to facilitate transportation. However, recent reports have varied greatly regarding the revised flight schedule, causing many people to misunderstand the truth. Yesterday, a reporter interviewed Mr. Li Jingcong, the general manager of the company, about this matter. It was learned that the company's current flights, except for the one from Shanghai via Nanjing, Zhengzhou, and Luoyang to Chengdu Jianming, which still flies as usual every Tuesday and Friday and returns every Thursday and Sunday, the northbound flights also connect in Zhengzhou every Tuesday and Friday, flying directly to Beiping via Taiyuan. On Wednesdays, they fly from Beiping via Baotou directly to Ningxia and return from Ningxia via Baotou to Beiping on the same day. On Thursdays and Sundays, they fly south from Beiping via Taiyuan to Zhengzhou, connecting with the eastbound flights from Chengdu Jianming to return to Shanghai. Therefore, except for Xi'an and Lanzhou, which are temporarily difficult to fly to, all other places can still be reached without obstruction, and it is possible to reach Taiyuan and Beiping from Shanghai on the same day. It is also possible to reach Baotou, Ningxia, and other places before noon on the designated days, which is more convenient than before.

Ministry of Finance Responds to Chamber of Commerce: Import Tax on Guangdong Foreign Rice; Cannot Be Exempted Immediately 168

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce received a reply from the Ministry of Finance yesterday: "To the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, we have reviewed the telegram of Geng. The foreign rice tax was originally established to protect domestic agricultural products. This year, Hunan, Jiangxi, Anhui and other provinces have reported good harvests, with surplus grain to supply the needs of Guangdong Province. It is not appropriate to exempt the foreign rice tax immediately, which would hinder the sale of domestic rice. We have already telegraphed the Guangdong Provincial Government to investigate. However, Guangdong Province has always been a rice-deficient area, and this year's summer floods and autumn droughts have made the shortage of food even greater than in previous years. You should immediately inform all merchants to transport rice produced in Hunan, Jiangxi, and Anhui to Guangdong in a steady stream to provide relief, so as to prevent the people of Guangdong Province from being panicked about food, and to assist the government's intention to protect domestic products. This is our earnest hope. Ministry of Finance (seal)."

竊佔墳地毀掘祖墳　胡與元等被控　法院裁定刑事停止審判　先向民庭起訴確認產權 174

Hu Yuanyuan and others are accused of illegally occupying and destroying ancestral graves. The court ruled that the criminal trial be suspended and that a civil lawsuit be filed first to confirm property rights.

Wang Fuquan, a local, retained lawyer Tang Xingjian to file a complaint with the Criminal Division of the Second Special District Court, accusing Hu Xingyuan of No. 305, Baier Road, and local leader Xu Wenquan (mentioned in the document) of colluding to illegally occupy a cemetery, destroy ancestral graves, and abandon remains, requesting investigation and return of the coffins. It was stated that their ancestor purchased four plots of land from Zhu Yueqing at the intersection of Shijian Road and Lafayette Road, located at No. 711, Tujingziwei, Section 1, Bao 27, during the third month of Guangxu 23, where eight ancestral coffins were buried. Now, local leader Xu Wenquan, Hu Xingyuan, and others had illegally occupied the land, destroyed the graves, and discarded all coffins and remains in the public cemetery. The court, based on the complaint, opened a hearing yesterday with Judge Sun Penghanzhuan. The defendant, Xu Wenquan, refused to receive the summons and did not appear because of a mistake in his name. Hu Xingyuan arrived with his defense lawyer, Wang Jian'e. The plaintiff testified about the previous situation and presented the purchase contract and field registration photos as evidence. The defendant, Hu Xingyuan, stated that the land was purchased by his late father, totaling three plots, and passed on to his sister, Hu Zhiyi. At that time, only a blank contract was given to her. Now, the blank contract was entrusted to Zhu Guiqing to apply to the Land Bureau for a land license, but Zhu lost the original contract and forged a false contract, which has been sued in the District Court. As for the excavated coffins, they were twelve coffins of his own ancestors, but there were two temporary coffins on the ground that no one claimed. A notice was posted asking people to claim them, but no one came to claim them after more than a month, so he entrusted the charity hall to collect them for burial and did not abandon them. The court, after reviewing the statements, ruled that both parties were contesting property rights, so it suspended the criminal trial and directed the plaintiff to file a lawsuit in the Civil Division to confirm property rights before proceeding with the criminal case, and then adjourned the court.

The content of each article is exceptionally substantial, and the writing is particularly valuable. As for the magazine's index of essential articles, this issue covers a total of 240 magazines and 7 supplements, comprising 597 volumes and 3,709 entries, with extremely rich materials. The end of the volume includes a table of contents for Volume 7 and a general classification table for the index of essential articles from Issues 1 to 10 of the upper volume. This issue contains over 110 pages, but the price has not been increased. Page 17

Popular Lecture

Mozi Rejects Chu to Save Song 194

— Yan Shu

——Saving a Country Requires Strength, Not Empty Words——

"Alas, it's really not good to be a weak country!" One night, Mozi sat alone in his small room, sighing at the candle flickering by the window, about to be blown out by the howling wind. As he spoke, he rose and piled many books high, covering a large hole in the window leaf, preventing the wind from blowing in.

He was a man of the Song state in the Warring States period. Unfortunately, at that time, hegemony was rampant. The strong attacked the weak, and the majority sought to annex the minority, often leading to massacres throughout cities and fields. He was a man of benevolence and could not bear to see such tragic massacres, so he advocated "non-aggression." He knew that war led to a lack of love, so he advocated "universal love." He saw that mutual love was mutually beneficial, but unfortunately, the world was blinded by selfish desires and did not understand this principle, so he traveled tirelessly to various countries to promote his doctrine of universal love. He was now going to the state of Qi to promote his doctrine of universal love. From Song to Qi, it was necessary to pass through the state of Lu. He did not want to disturb the people of Lu by greeting him, so he quietly hid in a small inn. He was planning to set off for Qi tomorrow when he suddenly heard the news that the state of Chu was about to attack the state of Song. In that case, he had no choice but to turn back and save his country first.

He sat anxiously, waiting for daybreak to open the city gates and start his journey. He pondered, and could not help but hate Gongshu Ban, the culprit who helped with the war. He still remembered clearly the words he had spoken with Ban in the state of Chu last month. It was a boring afternoon on a rainy day. Mozi visited Ban, and Ban kept him for dinner. After dinner, they began to talk like this:

"I am so proud. The military equipment I have made for fighting on ships is so good. The state of Yue really saw me defeat them!" Ban said gleefully, wiping his mouth and smiling at Mozi.

"With your skills, wouldn't it be great if you wholeheartedly helped your ancestral country (Ban was from the state of Lu) to escape the oppression of the state of Qi?" Mozi said, both as a loyal admonition and as a mockery.

"Um—" Ban blushed, unable to speak. After a while, he said, "Lu is too small, and there is no place for heroes to use their talents. How can you blame me for leaving it?"

"According to what you say, it is difficult for people to . If a country cannot get the love of its people because it is small, if this trend continues, in the future, everyone will only know selfishness, and I am afraid that weak children and elderly parents will not be cared for. What kind of world would that be?" Mozi was a little angry.

Ban sneered, "Sir, you are talking about benevolence and righteousness again! Let me ask you, my naval battle has hooks to grab and resist. Does your benevolence and righteousness also have hooks to grab and resist?"

"Why not? My hooks to grab and resist of benevolence and righteousness are much better than your hooks to grab and resist of naval battle. I use love to grab and respect to resist. If you don't use love to grab, you won't get people to be close to you; if you don't use respect to resist, you will provoke people to be familiar and disrespectful with you. If you are familiar but not close, it will lead to separation. So mutual benefit is the same. Today, if you use hooks to grab people, people will also use hooks to grab you; if you use resistance to resist people, people will also use resistance to resist you. So mutual grabbing and mutual resistance are the same as mutual harm. Therefore, my hooks to grab and resist of benevolence and righteousness are better than your hooks to grab and resist of naval battle." Mozi's words were very reasonable, and Ban could not refute him. After a long time , he never thought that this time he would actually make siege ladders for the King of Chu, preparing to attack Song.

This time, Mozi still decided to reason with Ban. He set off from the state of Lu, eager to save Song, and did not rest all the way, running for ten days and ten nights. His feet were broken, but he didn't care. Seeing that there was too much bleeding, he tore off a piece of clothing from his body to . With great difficulty, he ran to Yingdu to find Ban. Seeing Mozi coming fiercely, Ban knew that he had something to say, and quickly asked, "Sir, are you here? What do you want to tell me?"

Mozi gasped a few times before saying, out of breath, "There are several people in the north who have insulted me, and I want to ask you to kill them." Ban helped Mozi sit down, looking displeased. Mozi said, "If this is successful, I will reward you with ten pieces of gold."

"I am righteous in not killing people."

Hearing these words, Mozi was very moved. He quickly got up and bowed twice, expressing his sympathy for Ban, and then said very seriously, "Please listen to me for a few words: I heard in the north that you have already made siege ladders and are about to attack the state of Song. What crime has Song committed? The state of Jing, that is, the state of Chu, has excess land but insufficient people. Killing what is insufficient to fight for what is excess cannot be called wisdom; attacking the innocent Song cannot be called benevolence; knowing it is wrong but not arguing strongly cannot be called loyalty; arguing strongly but failing cannot be called strong righteousness; not killing the few but killing the many cannot be called knowing the class."

Hearing Mozi's words, Ban expressed his conviction. Mozi said, "Then, you ."

"That won't work, because I have already told the king about the plan to attack Song."

"Then, why not introduce me to the king?"

Ban immediately agreed. Mozi quickly took out an old dress from his clothing package and put it on, buttoning one or two buttons haphazardly, and then followed Ban to court to see the King of Chu. They didn't talk for a few words before Mozi directly asked the King of Chu, " someone who does not want his own painted carriage, but wants to steal his neighbor's broken cart; does not want his own brocade, but wants to steal his neighbor's short felt jacket; does not want his own rice and meat, but wants to steal his neighbor's bran. What kind of person does Your Majesty think this is?"

"This person must have a stealing disease," the King of Chu replied without thinking.

Mozi immediately seized the opportunity to say directly, "The land of Jing is five thousand li square, while the land of Song is only five hundred li square. This is like the comparison between a painted carriage and a broken cart. Jing has Yunmeng (in today's Jianli and Shishou counties in Hubei), full of rhinoceroses, rhinoceroses, deer, and deer, and the fish, turtles, and turtles of the Jianghan River are the richest in the world. As for Song, it is even inevitable that there are no crucian carp. This is like the comparison between rice and meat and bran. Jing has tall pines, catalpa, and other large trees, while Song has no large trees. This is like the comparison between brocade and short felt jackets. Today, Your Majesty's attack on Song, I think, also belongs to this kind of behavior."

"Yes! Yes! You are right. " The King of Chu nodded and said, "But Gongshu Ban is the most skillful person in the world. He made a siege ladder for me, and I will definitely be able to capture Song ."

At this time, Mozi also knew that those who were deceived by profit and desire could not be persuaded with righteousness, and he could not but propose his final effective method, strength, to control the King of Chu's ambition to invade. So he asked to compare each other's attack and defense strategies. They performed in front of the King of Chu. Mozi took off his belt and used it as a city, and broke chopsticks as military equipment. Ban used nine kinds of maneuvers to attack the city, and Mozi also used nine kinds of maneuvers to defend against the enemy. As a result, Ban's siege equipment, such as siege ladders, battering rams, flying stones, and crossbows, were all used up, but he still could not break through Mozi's defense line. It was obvious that Ban had lost. But he refused to admit defeat, and said maliciously, "I know how to win you, but I won't say it." Mozi saw through Ban's trick and smiled, "I know what you want to do to win me, but I won't say it."

The King of Chu was very surprised and asked Mozi what he knew. Mozi said, "Gongshu Zi's intention is just to kill me. He thinks that if he kills me, the state of Song will definitely have no one to defend it, and he can break through it; but he doesn't know that my disciples Lihua Li and others, three hundred in number, have already taken my defensive equipment and are waiting for the Chu army on the walls of Song. Even if you kill me, Song still cannot be captured."

"Yes! Yes! That's a good idea! Then I won't attack the state of Song anymore." The King of Chu said very firmly.

Ban was still not at ease and secretly sent people to the state of Song to inquire. Sure enough, the state of Song was prepared. Attacking a prepared country is a great taboo in military law, so the King of Chu had no choice but to withdraw the order to attack.

Complete Loyalty and Complete Faith 195

— Li Su

A story from the Roman-Carthaginian Wars

(Regulus was a great general of Rome, captured by the Carthaginians and made a prisoner. The beginning of this story is: Several Carthaginian leaders went to the prison to visit Regulus. They wanted Regulus to ask Rome to sue for peace.)

One, a prison cell in a Carthaginian prison

(Regulus): Gentlemen, the prison guard told me you wanted to talk to me.

(A): Yes, Regulus, we hope to end this current war because both sides have suffered significant loss of life. We have come up with a plan to negotiate peace with Rome. We have come to you hoping you can help us implement it.

(Regulus): Sir, why talk to me about peace and war? How can I help you? Am I not a defeated general and your prisoner?

(A): We are confident that your Roman compatriots do not know the seriousness of the situation in Africa. If they know that you have been defeated and are a prisoner, we believe they will welcome an opportunity to negotiate peace with us.

(Regulus): Sir, I believe Rome will fight. I know my country will not cease fighting until Carthage is overthrown. Why would we negotiate peace with you?

(B): When your compatriots understand that you are our prisoner, and your troops, at least those remaining, are in our control, and Carthage is now safe from Roman attack, you need not affirm that they will agree with you.

(Regulus): What you have heard is true, but in my country, people greater than Regulus are prepared and happy to die for Rome. My hope is that the misfortune of the current situation will not last long. But Carthaginians, what do you want me to do?

(A): We are willing to give you freedom, to let you go to Rome. However, there are two conditions, unless you agree to fulfill these terms we cannot let you go.

(Regulus): Then let me know. I need to know your purpose before I can decide whether to agree or not.

(A): We want you to agree that as soon as you arrive in Rome, you will immediately report to the Roman people the losses of this disastrous battle in which you were captured. You must especially report how many soldiers were killed and how many were captured. When they hear this report from Regulus' mouth, they will no longer be able to doubt, so they will not fail to understand that Rome has failed in this war.

(Regulus): What is the second condition?

(B): If the Romans refuse to sue for peace after hearing your report, you must agree to return to Carthage.

(Regulus): I am very willing to agree to these two things. I will report the losses of this campaign and mention the exact number of those killed and captured. And, if after my report, the Roman leaders are unwilling to negotiate peace, I promise you with the reputation of a Roman general that I will definitely return to Carthage.

(B): Agreed. We will report the results of our conversation to the Carthaginian government tomorrow morning. You will be free to take the first ship sailing to Rome.

(Regulus): Thank you, gentlemen. Good night.

Carthaginians: Good night, Regulus.

Two, in Rome

(Regulus and several leaders of the Roman government and army are sitting in his house.)

(Regulus): Welcome to my home, friends.

Roman A: Regulus, it is very gratifying to have you back in Rome. Rome does not often have the opportunity to see her generals. The Carthaginian War has left many of our best soldiers in Africa. I hear you have brought us news from Carthage.

(Regulus): What you have heard is true, gentlemen. I have returned home to report that the war in Africa is currently not in our favor. Rome was defeated in the last battle I participated in. My entire army was either killed or became prisoners. I myself was captured and imprisoned in Carthage. And I promised the Carthaginians to tell the Roman people about the seriousness of the war situation. They also told me to convey that if the Romans sue for peace, the Carthaginians are willing to negotiate a peace treaty.

(B): Peace! You, Regulus, a soldier, come to us to talk about making peace with the enemy?

(Regulus): Indeed. The Carthaginians sent me for this purpose. I have now fulfilled my promise. But now that I have reported, I am willing to advise you as a Roman general. May I?

(A): Of course, Regulus. Say as much as you like. We want to hear everything you have to say.

(Regulus): I strongly advise my country not to consider any peace treaties. Rome has failed several times, and at present our forces in Africa cannot conquer Carthage. All this is very true. But the Carthaginians have suffered significant losses and are gradually growing tired of the war. I think they are proposing a peace treaty to us because they are afraid of the future.

(B): This is really good news, Regulus. Here in Rome, it is very difficult to know for sure what the situation is in Africa. And it's hard to know who to believe. So you advise us to continue this war?

(Regulus): No matter what, just keep going. If we continue this war a little longer, Carthage will fall into our hands.

(A): I wish to express my gratitude on behalf of myself and the Roman government for what you have said. You have made our responsibilities clear to us.

Three, back at the same place the next day

(As Regulus is talking to his family, several Romans walk in.)

(B): I have come to speak on behalf of the people and leaders of Rome. You should immediately lead one of the new armies we are preparing to send to Africa. This is their unanimous hope. Your long experience and full understanding of the war situation in Africa make you the only person to bear this responsibility.

(Regulus): I am sorry to tell you that what you propose is impossible.

(A): Impossible! Why?

(Regulus): Because I must return tomorrow.

His wife: Return to Carthage? Ah, Regulus, I can't let you leave us again. Look at your children here! I beg you to think of them before you decide.

(A): Return to Carthage! That is too foolish. If you go back and our government refuses to negotiate peace, what will happen to you?

(Regulus): I know very well that my country will not negotiate peace. In any case, I have already promised that if Rome refuses to sue for peace, I will immediately return to Carthage.

(Wife): That means you will definitely die, Regulus.

(Regulus): I have known the meaning of my actions since I left Carthage. But I hope to say goodbye to my children, let my wife know that I expect her to be a brave person like a Roman woman should be, and Rome should continue to fight. I firmly believe that in a few months, Carthage will become ours.

(B): Brave Regulus! The Roman people will never forget your name.

(Regulus): What I ask is that Rome treat my wife and children well, so that they will never lack money and friends. Now, goodbye my compatriots! It's getting late, and before I leave, I have many words to say to my wife and children.

Romans: Good night, Regulus. Everything you have said will be conveyed to the people of Rome.

Four, Regulus returns to Carthage

What remains to be said is that Regulus fulfilled his promise. He returned to Carthage, while Rome continued to fight. When Rome refused to negotiate peace, Regulus was brutally murdered by the Carthaginians. But in the end, Rome won the war. Better than that, history remembers Regulus for sacrificing his life for keeping faith with an enemy.

The Ending of the Northern Song Dynasty and the Lessons of its Fall 196

— Da Chuan

— One of the Records of Laughable Matters in Reading History

Among the emperors of fallen dynasties, the tragic circumstances of Emperor Huizong and Emperor Qinzong of the Northern Song Dynasty were perhaps the most extreme. Historians often attribute the humiliation suffered by these two emperors and the downfall of the Northern Song Dynasty to the signs of decline in the Northern Song, and its inability to resist the massive southward advance of the Jin army. While this is historically accurate, the demise of the Northern Song also stemmed from the self-inflicted humiliation of Emperor Huizong and Emperor Qinzong, and their seeking their own destruction.

During the reign of Emperor Huizong, after the Jin people destroyed the Liao dynasty, their national power was strong. Although Emperor Huizong, as agreed, acquired the cultural artifacts and institutions of Yanjing (present-day Beijing), they had already been looted by the Jin people and were empty. At the same time, the Song had to annually pay the Jin dynasty one million strings of cash, and 200,000 bolts each of silver and silk as tax revenue collected from Yanjing. Later, Emperor Huizong repeatedly broke the agreement and initiated hostilities, which led to the Jin army marching south to demand justice, prompting Emperor Huizong's abdication and Emperor Qinzong's succession. Later, 60,000 Jin soldiers besieged Bianjing (present-day Kaifeng), while the Song had more than 200,000 troops ready to come to the capital's defense. However, they refused to adopt Li Gang's proposal for a decisive battle, and instead dismissed him to appease the Jin. Although he was temporarily reinstated at the request of the university students, the result was a humiliating peace, ceding three towns, paying huge amounts of money, and sending princes and ministers as hostages, while respectfully addressing the Jin ruler as "Uncle." This opened a rare chapter of shame in history.

After such a severe and devastating blow, Emperor Qinzong repeatedly broke the alliance. Therefore, the Jin army launched another major southward invasion. Jin general Nianhan led his troops across the river and besieged Bianjing. Soon, he again garrisoned troops, demanding money and land for peace, and sent spies to weaken the Song army. At that time, the ministers of the court lacked wisdom and were divided between advocating for peace and war, unable to reach a consensus! In the end, both the rulers and the subjects sought only temporary security and did not regard the Jin as a threat. Later, the Jin army marched south again, and Bianjing was captured for the second time. At that time, only three or four out of ten soldiers in the capital were capable of fighting, and they foolishly listened to the sorcerer Guo Jing's incantations, opened the gates to welcome the enemy, and hastened their own defeat. "Records of Night Talks Avoiding the Enemy" described the event: "Initially, when the capital was besieged, the court was eager to appoint generals. There was Guo Jing, originally a soldier in the Dragon Guard Camp of the Palace Guards, who was widely rumored to be able to use the Six Jia magic, to capture Nianhan alive and sweep away the remaining enemies without a trace. The court deeply believed in this." It also said, "The people he recruited were all idle men from the marketplace, of all kinds, not caring whether they were skilled in riding or archery, only choosing those whose years and fates matched the Six Jia... Guo Jing spoke and laughed freely, like a man of Dao, and chose a date to send out troops, promising peace." This kind of sorcery was very similar to the Boxer Rebellion during the Gengzi Incident, and its harm to the country and the people was indescribable. "Records of Night Talks Avoiding the Enemy" also said: "On the 25th day, the Xuanhua Gate was opened wide, and Guo Jing led his troops out... The Jin soldiers advanced in two wings, cheering loudly, crushing the front vehicles, sweeping them away as if cutting grass. Those behind were jealous and dragged them away... The soldiers defending the city and the common people in front caused the city to fall. Anger filled their hearts."

After the fall of Bianjing, Nianhan sent envoys to seek a peace treaty with the two emperors as prisoners, and to discuss the issue of land. All the cultural relics and books of the court were looted. At that time, it was snowing heavily in the capital, and the price of rice soared. Starved corpses filled the roads, and the Jin soldiers continued their large-scale looting. The number of people who died or were injured was countless. The tragedy of the fallen country was such.

The two emperors traveled north, suffering all kinds of human misery, even to the point of dying on the road or being killed. Later generations who read history cannot help but sigh and shed tears for them. Volume one of "Records of the Southern Remnants" stated: "When the two emperors' carriages arrived at the Jin camp, tens of thousands of common people blocked the carriages, wailing and refusing to let them pass. The emperors also wept." It also stated: "The two emperors and two empresses were all squatting in the mud, their food was coarse, their appearance was dark and haggard, their eyes were dim. The Supreme Emperor mistakenly fell into it, and they barely managed to pull him out. Empress Zheng also fell and injured her foot." It also stated: "The two emperors were imprisoned by the Jin people. In the middle of the day, they only received four bean cakes, which were divided among four people." The circumstances of the once noble emperors after the fall of their country cannot be expressed with mere tears of sorrow.

Volume two of "Records of the Southern Remnants" stated: "The soldiers tied the two emperors and two empresses in the courtyard and urinated and defecated on them." It also stated: "The two empresses were barefoot and unable to walk. Even when riding horses, their feet were covered in sores, and their flesh was thin and wasted. The two emperors were also withered and did not resemble living beings. They were scolded and whipped by the guards, with no way to die." It also stated: "The Jin ruler entered the palace, and attendants held the knees of the two emperors and empresses, kneeling on the ground. They all bowed twice." It also stated: "The attendants punched their mouths, causing them to bleed and their teeth to break, and then dragged them away. They were then brought into the front room and bound with ropes. The emperor wept without making a sound."

The humiliation of the fallen emperors had reached its extreme, but the misfortune of Emperor Huizong and Emperor Qinzong did not end there. The record of their circumstances of dying on the road or being killed is unbearable to witness: "Looking into the earthen pit, they saw that the Supreme Emperor was stiff and dead. The young emperor wailed loudly. The attendants led the local people to pierce the Supreme Emperor's corpse with wood, burn it halfway and extinguish it with water, and then discard the corpse into the pit." The tragic death of Emperor Huizong made Emperor Qinzong even more grief-stricken. "Stealing Feelings and Continuing Records" stated, "Some said that the young emperor wept and said, 'My father fell into a pit and drowned, my mother was buried by the roadside, my wife was wrapped in a bamboo mat, no different from the death of dogs and pigs! I don't know what will happen to me? If I die, it may not be different from this.'" Indeed, Emperor Qinzong's grief was no different from his anticipation of his tragic death, and his death was even more tragic. "Stealing Feelings and Continuing Records" also stated: "In the sixth year of Zhenglong, the Jin ruler Liang hosted a banquet for the princes and ministers in the military training hall and ordered the emperor and the Marquis of Binhai to play Cuju (ancient Chinese football). After the game, hundreds of Hu cavalrymen came from the corner of the field and charged directly in front of the emperor. A man in Jie clothing shot Yanxi through the heart and killed him under the horse. The emperor saw this, turned pale, and fell off his horse. Another man in purple clothing shot the emperor with an arrow. The emperor died, his body was not collected, but trampled into the ground by horses. The emperor was sixty years old when he died, the misfortune of the horse's feet."

After the fall of the Northern Song Dynasty, the two emperors and two empresses died in this way, leaving behind a tearful and bloody mark of humiliation and forbearance in history, forever serving as a lesson for those who lose their countries in later generations.

How to Study Philosophy (V) 197

— Yan Yilin

Written by Wang Te-fu, published by Sanjiang Bookstore

7. Steps for conducting research: The steps for studying philosophy should begin with the study of generalized, abstract problems, that is, from the study of epistemology and methods of cognition. This is the study of the core of philosophy. Because philosophy originally absorbed the achievements of specialized sciences to build its foundation and enrich its content, its research must move from generalized, abstract research to specialized, concrete research. However, philosophical research only takes the study of specific objects as one stage of the research process. It must return from the study of concrete individual problems to the study of general, abstract problems; abstract general laws from the study of realistic objects of various parts, and create general conclusions that can be common to the entire universe, thus constructing a general worldview. In addition, the research on various theoretical models in philosophy should also adopt such a process and route. In short, whether studying philosophical problems themselves or studying various theoretical models of philosophy, one must adopt the method of moving from generalized and abstract research to specialized and concrete research, and then to generalized and abstract research. This return is not a simple regression, but a research method that moves towards a higher stage of development, which is the dialectical research method.

Yuan Changying's "Peacock Flies Southeast" and Others 198

— Feng

"Peacock Flies Southeast"

(1) Creative Motivation and Writing Attitude

Using the marriage tragedy of Lan Zhi and Zhong Qing in the ancient poem "Peacock Flies Southeast" as a drama theme, as early as fourteen years ago, the drama "Peacock Flies Southeast" in five acts, collectively created by the fourth-grade students of the Chinese Department of Beijing Women's Higher Normal School, was published by the New China Drama Association. Yuan Changying's "Peacock Flies Southeast" and other one-act plays, published by the Commercial Press, were written ten years later and published in 1979. At the same time, there was also Xiong Foxi's one-act play "Lan Zhi and Zhong Qing." With the same theme, the creative focus of the playwrights may not be exactly the same, which is a fact. Regarding this point, as well as the techniques and methods of each play, I will discuss it in another article.

As for Yuan's own central viewpoint in creating this play, she herself has clearly stated in the preface:

"... I have learned that there is always a psychological background to the relationship between people. Jiao's mother's dislike of Lan Zhi is naturally a psychological effect. Based on my personal experience and daily observations, I speculate that most of the discord between mothers-in-law and daughters-in-law is due to "jealousy." I am not saying that there is any secret behavior between the mother and son that makes her jealous of the daughter-in-law... If she encounters someone who is still young, passionate, and unfortunately a widow, the tragedy of Zhong Qing and Lan Zhi will inevitably occur."

Most authors who write family tragedies tend to focus on fate. Family tragedies are the result of people fighting against fate. Yuan's writing of "Peacock Flies Southeast" can eliminate this prejudice and create a unique view of psychological effects, which is indeed a profound understanding. Based on this point of view, the author has made great efforts to study the social customs of the time in order to achieve complete success, which is especially commendable. Because new attempts can hold a serious and non-casual attitude, which is rare. This should be especially mentioned when writing this article.

(2) Synopsis of Each Act

The whole play is divided into three acts

Act One: Zhong Qing before marriage is ill because he misses Lan Zhi. His mother tries to comfort him with love. The neighbor comes to talk and persuades the mother to quickly complete the marriage for her son to dispel bad luck. The mother reveals her thoughts, fearing that after her son marries a wife, she will be placed behind her. The matchmaker comes and urges the marriage. Zhong Qing hears the good news and recovers quickly. This shows the factors of the widowed mother's love for her son and jealousy of the future daughter-in-law's position.

Act Two: After Lan Zhi's marriage, the couple's love is pleasant, but they cannot get the mother's forgiveness. She suffers daily abuse and excessive labor, but she endures without complaint. The mother does not allow her to stay in the room, angry that her son loves his wife more than his mother, and finally sends Lan Zhi back to her mother's house.

Act Three: A scene on the outskirts of the road. The news of Lan Zhi's remarriage comes, and they are forced to die together with Zhong Qing, and the mother goes insane. This completes a great human tragedy.

(3) Characters

The existing characters have not been greatly increased or decreased here. Count:

"Jiao's mother, Grandmother

Lan Zhi, Matchmaker

Zhong Qing, Hua'er

Young uncle, Maid"

The roles have reached the most economical point. Of course, economy can be a harmful existence in some dramas.

Boatman 199

— Lin Jia

The sea is tired, like a fierce lion, retracting its wild roar, calming its anger, and sleeping in the gentle breeze.

Who knows how long it will sleep? At this time tomorrow, will the sea be a dreamlike smile? Or an angry roar?

The boatman raises the sail, leans against the ship, and gently exhales the day's hardships from the fine smoke of his pipe.

Further away are the white clouds. His hometown is still beyond the white clouds, where his wife and young children are, the cradle of dreams and hopes.

There is no sorrow in life, only the interweaving of sweat and waves. Who has so much free time to indulge in distant memories?

If only wings could grow from his back, so he could fly freely like a seagull!

The smoke curls, and beyond the smoke is a gray mist. On the other side of the lighthouse, is it an island? Is it the endless blue sea? Or the longed-for land?

Mount Tai 200

— Zuo Rong

The train carried us to Tai'an, such a long and distant journey. Taking a rickshaw and walking was exhausting before we reached the right path up the mountain.

It was spring: the ground was covered with lush green grass and neatly growing wheat seedlings. The wind blew gently, creating ripples like water, which made people love it. The trees were showing new postures, and the lively atmosphere told people that they had awakened from the embrace of winter. The mountain scenery was very beautiful, making people think that what people said about Mount Tai was how good, how good, not exaggerated at all.

My younger brother started running and jumping as soon as he reached the First Heaven Gate, but I pulled him back. He was unhappy and pouted.

After passing a few old bent pine trees, apricot trees grew densely by the roadside. The mid-spring weather was the stage of youth at the bottom of the flowers – the flowers were blooming brilliantly, and butterflies and bees were flying in groups in the flowers, setting off the whole world into a poetic picture.

"Let's go, if you don't go, I'll run..."

My younger brother said, struggling to get out of my hands - run, we had no choice but to go. He was really annoying, jumping all the way, as if he didn't even know what he was going to do! Watching this person walking around noisily, and watching that person walking around noisily, and watching the immortal who has attained enlightenment – the dry bones and the fake head made into Sun Zhenren, he became interested, not only did he not walk around noisily, but his eyes stared straight at him - if the Taoist priest hadn't been watching there, he would have really stood up and touched him.

The waterfall under the Yunbu Bridge is really a beautiful picture, the water flows continuously from top to bottom, white like a silver chain. Sometimes the flow is too intense, and the splashed water stars are like silver shavings. There is light and sound, which makes people feel dazed there.

Along the way, children begging for money - some boys and some girls, all eight or nine years old, followed behind asking for money, shouting out skilled words in a clumsy Tai'an accent.

"Give me some money, young master, young lady! Give me some money..."

My younger sister and brother also shouted along, imitating very well, and even the children begging for money laughed.

The South Heaven Gate is like a temple, located so high in the sky that it is surprisingly high, making people worry first - how difficult it is to walk the "Eighteen Bends"! The road is a steep stone staircase, standing like a ladder to heaven. It makes people think: "No wonder it is called the Heaven Gate"!

In the house near the gate that used a large bowl for children to eat as a sign, after eating something and drinking a pot of tea, Dad bought some things for worshipping the gods and went to the top again.

In the temple of the Goddess of Mount Tai, after burning incense, Dad kowtowed to the statue of the god, touched his younger brother's head, and said softly and quietly:

"Yes, he is already so big"!

My younger brother just stared at the statue of the god, he didn't understand why?

I laughed at my younger brother -: This is the child that the Goddess of Mount Tai gave to Dad! An inexplicable mysterious meaning enveloped my heart.

In the shop where we had dinner, Dad woke us up in the middle of the night. The sky was still hanging with sparse stars, and we ran to the mountain. On the high hill behind the Wanghai Stone, we stared blankly at the foot of the mountain to the east. The surrounding mountains were all covered with the breath of smoke and fog. The wind brought the cold air of mid-spring to people, making them shiver.

Commentary

Education and Nobility 201

— Shi Ji

Education is said to be a "noble" undertaking. Judging from the respect that country people have for scholars, it does indeed seem to be so. I don't know about other places, but in Shanghai, I feel that the word "noble" should be discounted a bit. The reason is not that Shanghai is a cultural center and there are too few places where scholars are respected, so the price drops automatically. It is actually because there are too many strange phenomena that the price has to drop.

At the beginning of each school season, advertisements for enrollment printed with Western-style houses can often be seen, and there seems to be wording like "thoughtful," which makes people very puzzled. What is even more puzzling are those so-called "alley primary schools" with one floor and one bottom. A house with one floor and one bottom has to be divided into several classrooms, teacher's lounges, and even a playground. Besides marveling at the precision of the calculation, there is nothing else to say.

But after a long time, knowing more, it becomes clear that those "alley primary schools" might as well be called "Confucius Says Shops" to be clear and straightforward, and it also turns out to be ordinary. Even the news about "schools and gambling tables" feels natural, since it is a "shop."

However, I still cannot help but be in awe of the news that someone filed a lawsuit because they were identified as a student. According to reports: The principal of Mushi English Night School was sued because "the school published a realistic enrollment advertisement stating that the plaintiff was a student, stating that after receiving education from this school, he was the principal of Mushi Night School, etc., but the plaintiff was a graduate of St. Francis." Therefore, he believed that it "affected his reputation and career" and filed a criminal self-suit, with an attached civil suit for 1,000 yuan. The other party, in addition to presenting various material and witness evidence to prove that the other party was indeed an English typing class student in the 19th year of the Republic of China, also filed a countersuit for slander, listing "betraying teachers" and other major crimes in the indictment.

What the result of this matter will be, the court will judge. But outside the scope of the law, one might as well talk about whether being someone's student "affects one's reputation and career"? And does publishing the student's promotion to principal in the enrollment advertisement also sufficiently prove the good achievements of the alma mater?

The principals probably admire Confucius, the "teacher of all generations," so Confucius said, "When three people walk together, there must be someone who can be my teacher." This shows that being a student does not "affect one's reputation and career." If Confucius were born in modern times, he might have gone to Mushi or Wushi Night School to take English lessons for the sake of need.

As for whether teachers are necessarily stronger than students? I remember that there is also a Chinese idiom called "The green comes from the blue but surpasses the blue," which shows that students are definitely not necessarily less successful than teachers, and the student's school is not necessarily weaker than the alma mater, which can also make people feel relieved. If teachers are always better than students, this world would never have gone from the Stone Age to the current Electric Age.

But why does one insist on identifying someone as a student, and the other insist on "betraying teachers"? To put it bluntly, it is very clear that both principals believe that teachers are necessarily superior to students.

Since schools take business as a premise, and peers are jealous of each other, the name of "teacher" and "student" is naturally something to be contended for, not to mention there are "tactics of using temptation, committing various acts of harming others and benefiting oneself" as a fuse?

But this also makes outsiders more clearly understand the so-called nobility of education!

My younger brother and sister couldn't see anything and were a little impatient—

"Let's go! Cold..."

Others

Imported White Sugar

In late July 1936, smuggling was rampant, causing immense losses to all legitimate merchants and even bringing them to the brink of bankruptcy. In a small market town along a railway line in Jiangnan, there was a Demao native goods store. The owner, Li Desheng, felt very pained that smuggling was rampant and no one was eating domestic sugar. Therefore, he invited his peers to discuss effective ways to stop smuggling. His daughter, Huaying, was studying in Shanghai and was now at home for the summer vacation. She helped her father explain the harm of smuggling to the nation and the country, and advised conscientious merchants not to smuggle goods. Everyone organized an anti-smuggling group and said that Shanghai students would come down today to help them check for smuggled goods. At the meeting, Boss Wang was the most vocal against smuggling and the most enthusiastic about anti-smuggling, but it was known that he was secretly colluding with small railway station staff to transport and sell large quantities of smuggled goods. On this day, the imported white sugar and rayon transported from Shanghai were indeed found by Huaying's classmates. She slipped away quietly when she heard the bad news at the meeting. At this time, everyone at the meeting was extremely angry, unanimously saying that smugglers are our enemies, they want to cause us all to die! We will never eat smuggled imported white sugar. Whoever sells, buys, or eats it is not Chinese!

Singing 205

Afterglow

The "Mimi Collection" magazine, Issue 29, published by the Yuanchang Radio Station in this city, has been published. It is rich in content, including popular songs, long novels, storytelling fragments, essays, drama scripts, etc. Each issue is sold separately for two cents. For mail orders, please send to Yuanchang Advertising Company Radio Station, No. 7, Lane 3, Caishi Road, Shanghai.

The Shanghai Radio Station of the Ministry of Communications (1300) invites Mr. Mao Guitang and Ms. Ru Meimei of Datong University to give a lecture on "About Home Economics" and "Transformation of Family Education" from 4:30 PM to 5:15 PM this afternoon. It is hoped that people from all walks of life will pay attention at that time.

Movies

"As You Like It" Premieres Tonight 207

The long-awaited literary masterpiece "As You Like It" has been scheduled to premiere tonight at 9:15 PM at the Grand Light Cinema. This is one of the most famous works of the great writer Shakespeare. Readers who have read Shakespeare's work know the story of this film. In terms of script preparation, this "As You Like It" brought to the screen retains the two major characteristics of literary films: first, the whole play is very faithful, it does not casually modify it like other literary films, so that they lose the original style and true essence: second, the dialogue of the characters in the play and the temperament of the whole play also maintain the original strong literary and poetic style. As for the leading actors, we dare to use the highest praise to introduce this European superstar - Elizabeth Bergner. In "As You Like It," she has a scene in almost every segment. Her superb, delicate, and warm acting skills, and her clear, flowing and rhythmic verses, are truly rare. In literary films, this is the most faithful and beautiful giant drama.

"Stolen Kisses" Screens at Greater Shanghai 208

The new film company jointly established by veteran film stars Mary Pickford and Lasky has released its first production, "Stolen Kisses," which is now showing at the Greater Shanghai Theater. The film is a very light-hearted comedy. All the details of the play begin with a mistaken kiss in the theater, which results in a court trial. The man says that seeing such a beautiful girl, he couldn't help but feel the desire in his heart; the woman also pretends to be serious, half-heartedly accepts, so it goes, the plot is unspeakably wonderful. The stars are Fredric March and Hollywood beauty Ida Lupino, the protagonist of "The Adventures of Robin Hood." In addition to the film's humorous plot and light-hearted dialogue, the several popular songs in it are also very beautiful and moving.

"One Night of Folly" Screens at Cathay 209

Starting today, the Cathay Theater is showing "One Night of Folly" Wives Never Know, starring the two major comedy stars, Charlie Ruggles and Marie Wilson. The film is produced by Paramount Pictures, and the plot is romantic and humorous, the performance is enthusiastic and compact, and it is indeed hilarious. These two stars are originally famous for acting in this kind of play, and they have made amazing gains in this film. In addition to the two of them, a famous comedian with a small mustache, Adolph Menjou, is also added, so the jokes are released non-stop like a string of beads.

Paris's Amazing Contribution 211

Columbia's production of "The Awful Truth" has been popular for a long time, with歌后Irene Dunne and 風流小生Cary Grant co-starring, it can be called a perfect match. The Paris Cinema on Avenue Joffre carefully selects films. On this Christmas holiday, to serve all people, the theater has recently selected a blockbuster that will make an amazing contribution, such as "Little Lord Fauntleroy," "San Francisco," "Mr. Deeds Goes to Town," "Spirit of Patriotism," etc., which will be shown in sequence. This Christmas, in order to please the children, a collection of the most exciting colorful cartoon comedies will be shown at 10:30 AM on the 25th and 26th, with a uniform price of 20 cents.

Giving Away Autographed Photos of Chen Juanjuan 212

Chen Juanjuan, China's only child star, once again took the lead in "Little Orphan Girl," performing with a new attitude, which caused a sensation across the country and bloomed a wonderful flower in the history of Chinese child stars. In the past two days, many people from all over the country have been asking for photos of Juanjuan. Juanjuan is extremely busy with filming and studying, and at the same time, there are too many people who want them, which is difficult to deal with, and it is impossible to send them one by one. Therefore, she entrusted the famous photographer Du Ao to take more than a hundred new poses of photos, and entrusted him to distribute them to all walks of life. Each photo is personally signed by Juanjuan, and a fee of five cents is charged for developing, printing, and postage. Those who love Juanjuan's art and do not yet have his photo can ask for it from Mr. Du Ao, No. 2954, Xiangyin Road, Jiangwan, Shanghai.
